Emergency Slaughter: When and How It Is Permissible
Rule and conditions for emergency slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for emergency slaughter and apply it by distinguishing between situations where standard slaughter is possible and where it is not.

Core Idea
Emergency slaughter is a substitute: valid only when standard slaughter is impossible.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi principle that governs emergency slaughter (dhabh al-idtirar). The central idea is that emergency slaughter is a substitute (badal) for the standard method (dhabh al-ikhtiyar). Consequently, it may only be used when one is genuinely unable to perform the standard cut between the collar and the jaws. We will see how this rule applies to domesticated animals, wild game, and animals that become uncontrollable. We will also touch on the disliked nature of causing extra pain, such as cutting the spinal cord prematurely.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of slaughter
Identify the standard method (throat cut between collar and jaws) and the emergency method (wounding any part to cause blood flow). Understand that emergency is a substitute.
The substitute is only invoked when the original is impossible.
2
State the core rule
Emergency slaughter is only resorted to when one is unable to perform standard slaughter. As long as standard is possible, emergency is not allowed.
This is based on the principle that a substitute cannot precede the original.
3
Apply to domesticated animals
For a tame animal (like a sheep or cow), standard slaughter is possible, so emergency slaughter is not permitted. Only if the animal bolts or falls into a well and cannot be caught does emergency become permissible.
The same applies to domesticated game.
4
Apply to wild animals
For wild animals that are generally not controllable, emergency slaughter is the default method: wounding in any part suffices.
If a wild animal is captured and can be slaughtered normally, standard method should be used.
5
Note the ethical ruling on al-nakh'
Cutting the spinal cord or breaking the neck before the animal dies (al-nakh') is makruh (disliked) because it causes unnecessary pain without benefit. However, the animal remains halal.
This is derived from the prohibition of causing unnecessary suffering to animals.

Principles of Hidayah, page 212. (21) The emergency slaughter is only resorted to when unable to perform the optional slaughter. Translation: Emergency slaughter will be resorted to when optional slaughter is impossible. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that emergency slaughter occurs when a person is unable to perform optional slaughter, but as long as he has power over optional slaughter, emergency slaughter is not permissible, because emergency slaughter is a substitute for optional slaughter, and the substitute is resorted to when a person is incapable of the original. The author of Hidayah, mentioning this principle, explains that a domesticated animal is slaughtered by optional slaughter, and a wild animal is slaughtered by emergency slaughter, i.e., by wounding it in any place. Because a person has power over optional slaughter of a domesticated animal, and when he has power over optional slaughter, emergency slaughter is not permissible. Therefore, emergency slaughter will not be permissible for domesticated game either. And a person is generally not able to perform optional slaughter of a wild animal, so wounding it in any part will effect slaughter. Similarly, if a domesticated animal bolts and cannot be controlled, or falls into a well and it becomes difficult to slaughter it by optional slaughter, then wounding it in any part of its body will effect slaughter. He said: (And what is domesticated from game, the emergency slaughter has passed as a substitute for optional, so there is no resorting to the former before inability of the latter, and this is the derivation of what is mentioned in the book. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Dhaba'ih, vol. 9, p. 497) His statement: (And what is domesticated from game, its slaughter is the slaughter because it can be slaughtered like a sheep. His statement: (And what is wild from livestock, its slaughter is by wounding and injuring. And the basis of this is that slaughter is of two types: optional and emergency. Whenever one is able to perform optional slaughter, emergency slaughter is not permissible for him, and when he is unable, emergency slaughter becomes permissible. So optional slaughter is between the collar and the jaws, and emergency slaughter is stabbing and injuring and causing blood to flow, and everything that is in a similar situation, from domesticated animals like camels if they bolt or something of them falls into a well and he cannot slaughter it, he stabs it in any place he can and it becomes permissible to eat it. Similarly, if a cow falls into a well and he cannot slaughter it, then its slaughter is by wounding as long as it does not hit the veins; on this the scholars are agreed because slaughter is impossible. As for a sheep, if it bolts in the desert, its slaughter is by wounding because he cannot get it. (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: Kitab al-Sayd wa al-Dhaba'ih, vol. 2, p. 183)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the principle of emergency slaughter (dhabh al-idtirar) as opposed to standard optional slaughter (dhabh al-ikhtiyar). The author begins by stating the core rule: emergency slaughter is resorted to only when one is unable to perform standard slaughter. The Urdu commentary explains that emergency slaughter is a substitute (na'ib) for standard slaughter, and a substitute is only used when the original is impossible. This is applied practically: domesticated animals (such as sheep or cows) must be slaughtered in the standard way—cutting the throat between the collar and the jaws—because one has control over them. Wild animals, or domesticated animals that have become uncontrollable (e.g., bolted or fallen into a well), may be slaughtered by wounding them in any part of the body, as standard slaughter is not possible. The text then quotes from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and Al-Inayah, emphasizing that any act during slaughter that causes unnecessary suffering (like cutting the spinal cord or breaking the neck before the animal dies) is makruh (disliked) because it involves harming the animal without benefit. This principle is derived from the hadith of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) prohibiting such practices. Thus, the passage covers both the rule of emergency slaughter and the recommended conduct to minimize pain.

Key Terms
ذكاة الاضطرار (dhabh al-idtirar): Emergency slaughter: slaughter by wounding in any part of the body when standard slaughter is impossible.
ذكاة الاختيار (dhabh al-ikhtiyar): Standard slaughter: cutting the throat between the collar and the jaws.
النخع (al-nakh'): Cutting the spinal cord or breaking the neck before the animal dies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is emergency slaughter (dhabh al-idtirar) permissible?
A) Whenever it is more convenient than standard slaughter.
B) Only when a person is unable to perform standard slaughter due to inability to control the animal.
C) For all wild animals, even if they can be captured and slaughtered normally.
D) Only for animals that have fallen into a well.

Key Takeaway
Emergency slaughter is a substitute for standard slaughter and is only valid when standard slaughter is genuinely impossible.

Sacrifice Not Obligatory on Father for Minor Child
Ruling stating that sacrifice is not obligatory on a father for his minor child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sacrifice (udhiyah) is not wajib on a father for his minor child and apply the principle that pure worship (qurbah mahdah) is not obligatory on one person due to another.

Core Idea
Sacrifice is not wajib on a father for his minor child because it is pure worship, unlike sadaqat al-fitr.

We often assume that a father must fulfill religious obligations on behalf of his minor children, as he does for their maintenance. However, the Hanafi school makes a critical distinction: pure acts of worship (qurbah mahdah) like sacrifice and Hajj cannot be transferred to another person. This lesson explores the ruling from Al-Hidayah and the underlying legal maxim that shapes the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that sacrifice (udhiyah) is not wajib on a father for his minor child. Recognize that this is a negative obligation (not wajib) on the father.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the legal maxim: 'al-asl fi al-qurb an la tajiba 'ala al-ghayr bi-sabab al-ghayr' – the principle in worship is that it should not be obligatory on another due to another.
This maxim is the foundation of the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Sacrifice is classified as pure worship (qurbah mahdah). Since it has no worldly cause, the maxim applies directly: it cannot become wajib on a father simply because of his child.
Compare with sadaqat al-fitr, which has a worldly cause (the child is under his support).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'is hold that a father may sacrifice on behalf of his child as a recommended act, but the Hanafi school maintains it is not wajib. The disagreement stems from how they define 'pure worship'.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is from Zahir al-Riwayah: sacrifice is only obligatory for oneself. Al-Marghinani and Al-Jawharah affirm this.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text

(۲۲) اَلْأَصْلُ فِي الْقُرْبِ أَنْ لَا تَجِبَ عَلَى الْغَيْرِ بِسَبَبِ الْغَيْرِ. ترجمہ: قربت میں اصل یہ ہے کہ غیر پر غیر کے سبب سے واجب نہ ہو۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عبادت محضہ میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ کسی اور کی وجہ سے دوسرے پر واجب نہ ہو، مثلاً زید پر حج فرض ہے تو زید کی وجہ سے عمر و پر فرض نہیں ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ باپ پر اولاد صغیر یعنی نابالغ بچے کی وجہ سے قربانی کرنا واجب نہیں ہے، چاہے بچہ کے پاس مال ہو یا نہ ہو، کیونکہ قربانی عبادت محضہ ہے، اور عبادت محضہ میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ غیر کی وجہ سے غیر پر واجب نہ ہو، لہذا قربانی میں بھی اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ بچے کی وجہ سے باپ پر واجب نہ ہو، برخلاف صدقہ فطر کے کہ وہ والد پر لازم ہے، اس لیے کہ اس کا سبب راس ہے جو موجود ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الأضحية، ج ۴ ص ۴۴۴
وفى ظاهر الرواية لا تجب إلا عن نفسه خاصة بخلاف صدقة الفطر لأن السبب هناك رأس یمونه ویلی عليه وهذه قربة محضة، والأصل في القرب أن لا تجب على الغير بسبب الغير. (الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الأضحية، ج ۲ ص۱۸۷)

Book of Sacrifice

(22) The principle in acts of worship is that they should not be obligatory on another due to another. Translation: The principle in worship is that it should not be obligatory on another due to another. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that in pure worship, the principle is that it should not be obligatory on another due to someone else. For example, if Zayd has Hajj as obligatory, it does not become obligatory on 'Amr due to Zayd. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is stating that sacrifice is not obligatory on a father due to his minor child, whether the child has wealth or not. Because sacrifice is pure worship, and in pure worship the principle is that it should not be obligatory on another due to another. Therefore, in sacrifice, the principle is that it should not be obligatory on the father due to the child, unlike sadaqat al-fitr which is incumbent on the parent because its cause is a head that he supports and has authority over. (Hidayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 4 p. 444) And in zahir al-riwayah, it is not obligatory except for himself specifically, unlike sadaqat al-fitr because the cause there is a head he supports and has authority over, while this is pure worship, and the principle in worship is that it should not be obligatory on another due to another. (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 2 p. 187)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof stating that the sacrifice (udhiyah) is not obligatory on a father for his minor child. The proof is the legal maxim: 'The principle in acts of worship is that they are not obligatory on one person due to another.' The author explains that pure worship (qurbah mahdah), such as sacrifice and Hajj, cannot be made obligatory on someone else because of another person. This is contrasted with sadaqat al-fitr, which is obligatory on the father for his minor child because its cause is the child being under his support (ra's yamunuhu). The ruling from Al-Jawharah confirms that in zahir al-riwayah, the sacrifice is only obligatory for oneself, not for one's dependents.

Key Terms
قربة محضة (qurbah mahdah): Pure act of worship with no worldly cause; its obligation is not transferred to another person.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan; it is wajib on a person for himself and for his dependents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is a father obligated to perform sacrifice (udhiyah) for his minor child?
A) Yes, if the child has wealth
B) Yes, always
C) No, because sacrifice is pure worship
D) No, only if the child is an adult

Key Takeaway
A father is not obligated to sacrifice for his minor child because sacrifice is pure worship; the principle is that pure worship is not transferred to another due to another.

The Maxim: Opinion Cannot Determine Fixed Shar'i Quantities
Legal maxim defining the limits of reason in fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal maxim regarding fixed quantities and apply it to examples such as nisab and days of sacrifice.

Core Idea
Fixed shar'i quantities are revealed, not reasoned — ra'y cannot set them.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal maxim that governs how we understand fixed quantities in Islamic law. The maxim holds that human reasoning has no jurisdiction over matters like the nisab of zakat or the days of sacrifice; these are determined solely by divine revelation. Understanding this principle prevents the misuse of qiyas in areas reserved for textual determination.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Maxim's Wording
Read the maxim in Arabic and Urdu. Note that 'al-ra'y' refers to personal opinion or independent reasoning, and 'al-maqadir' are the fixed quantities set by the Lawgiver.
The maxim is a complete sentence: 'Opinion does not guide to the quantities.'
2
Identify Examples of Fixed Quantities
The text mentions nisab of zakat and the days of sacrifice (from 10th to 12th Dhul Hijjah). Also consider other ta'abbudi quantities like number of rak'ahs, number of rounds in tawaf, etc.
These are matters of worship ('ibadat) where the details are established by revelation.
3
Recognize the Scope: What Cannot Be Analogized
The maxim applies to all quantities that are explicitly specified in the Quran or Sunnah and are not open to qiyas. This includes thresholds, time periods, and numbers.
Hanafi usul holds that qiyas does not operate in the presence of a text (nass).
4
Apply the Maxim to Prevent Analogical Reasoning
If someone tries to change the nisab of zakat by analogy to inflation, the maxim teaches that such reasoning is invalid because the quantity is fixed by revelation.
The principle is accepted by all Hanafis and most other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۳) الرَّأْيُ لَا يَهْتَدِي إِلَى الْمَقَادِيرِ .
ترجمہ: رائے مقادیر کی طرف رہنمائی حاصل نہیں کر سکتی۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جتنے بھی مقادیر شرع ہیں، مثلاً نصاب زکوۃ، ایام قربانی وغیرہ ، ان میں رائے اور قیاس نہیں چلتی بلکہ یہ سب سماع پر موقوف ہوتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ انتظار ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک قربانی یوم انحر

(23) Opinion cannot find guidance to quantities.
Translation: Opinion cannot guide to quantities.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that all quantities in sharia, such as the nisab of zakat, the days of sacrifice, etc., cannot be determined by opinion and analogy; rather, they all depend on divine revelation. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, expects that according to the Hanafis, the sacrifice on the day of Nahr... (Hidayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 4 p. 446)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qa'idah) stating that rational reasoning (ra'y) cannot discover the fixed quantities (maqadir) in Islamic law. Examples include the nisab for zakat and the specific days for sacrifice. These quantities are determined solely by textual revelation (sam') and are not subject to qiyas or independent reasoning. The author of Hidayah uses this maxim to emphasize that the days of sacrifice (from 10th to 12th of Dhul Hijjah) are fixed by revelation, not by human opinion.

Key Terms
المقادير الشرعية (al-maqadir al-shar'iyyah): Legal quantities specified by sharia, such as nisab, number of days, number of rak'ahs.
الرأي (al-ra'y): Personal opinion or rational reasoning; cannot determine fixed quantities in sharia.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim 'al-ra'yu la yahtadi ila al-maqadir', how are legal quantities in sharia determined?
A) By personal opinion
B) By analogy (qiyas)
C) By divine revelation (sam')
D) By consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Fixed quantities in sharia (such as nisab and days of sacrifice) are determined solely by revelation and cannot be altered by human reasoning.

The Principle: Shariah Quantities Are Known by Transmission (Sam')
Delivering the principle that opinion cannot determine Shariah quantities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that shariah quantities (maqadir) are determined solely by transmission (sam') and identify examples such as nisab and days of sacrifice.

Core Idea
Opinion cannot ascertain Shariah quantities — only the revealed sources can set them.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi usul principle: 'Al-ra'y la yahtadi ila al-maqadir' — personal opinion cannot guide to the divinely legislated quantities. In matters where Shariah specifies a number, measure, or time, human reasoning (ra'y) and analogy (qiyas) are invalid; only transmitted evidence (sam') is admissible. This principle governs rulings such as zakat nisab, fixed periods like iddah, and the days of sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core qa'ida
The passage opens with 'al-ra'y la yahtadi ila al-maqadir'. Recognize this as a legal maxim (qa'ida) that limits the role of human reasoning in fixed Shariah quantities.
Memorize this maxim — it is a key Hanafi usul principle.
2
Define 'maqadir shara'
Maqadir are specific quantities set by the Lawgiver, such as the nisab of zakat, the number of raka'at in prayer, the days of sacrifice, and the waiting period (iddah). They are not subject to human adjustment.
Contrast with 'ahkam' that may be derived via qiyas.
3
Distinguish sam' from ra'y
Sam' refers to knowledge derived from revelation (Quran, Sunnah) and authenticated reports of the Companions. Ra'y is personal opinion or independent reasoning. In maqadir, only sam' is valid.
Hanafis consider maqadir to be tawqifi (divinely set).
4
Apply to a familiar example
Consider the nisab of zakat: 200 dirhams or 5 wasaq. These numbers cannot be changed by qiyas; they are fixed by textual evidence. The same applies to the days of sacrifice.
This example is mentioned in the source text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرَّأْيُ لَا يَهْتَدِي إِلَى الْمَقَادِيرِ . ترجمہ: رائے مقادیر کی طرف رہنمائی حاصل نہیں کر سکتی۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جتنے بھی مقادیر شرع ہیں، مثلاً نصاب زکوۃ، ایام قربانی وغیرہ ، ان میں رائے اور قیاس نہیں چلتی بلکہ یہ سب سماع پر موقوف ہوتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ [؟] انتظار ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک قربانی یوم انحر اور دو دن بعد میں ، یعنی دس گیارہ، بارہ ذی الحجہ میں جائز ہے، جبکہ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یوم انحر کے تین دن بعد بھی قربانی جائز ہے یعنی تیرویں ذی الحجہ میں بھی۔ احناف کی دلیل ایام قربانی کے بارے میں یہ ہے کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمرو، حضرت ابن عباس اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہم فرماتے ہیں کہ ایام نحر تین دن ہیں اور ان میں افضل پہلا دن ہے، طرز استدلال اس طرح ہے کہ چونکہ ایام قربانی مقادیر شرع میں سے ہے اور مقادیر میں رائے نہیں چلتی، لہذا ایام قربانی کی تعیین میں بھی رائے نہیں چلے گی ، جب ایامِ قربانی میں رائے کا کوئی عمل دخل نہیں ہے تو اس کی تعیین سماع پر موقوف ہوگی۔ قال (وَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ إِلَخُ كَلَامُهُ وَاضِحٌ) (الهداية كتاب الأضحية، ج ۴ ص ۴۴۹)
Opinion cannot attain to the quantities. Translation: Opinion cannot guide to the quantities. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that whatever quantities are in the Shariah, such as the nisab of zakat, the days of sacrifice, etc., opinion and analogy do not apply to them, but rather they are all dependent on hearing (sam'). The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to indicate that according to the Hanafis, sacrifice is permissible on the day of sacrifice (yawm al-nahr) and the two days after, i.e., 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijja, whereas Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) says that sacrifice is permissible up to three days after yawm al-nahr, i.e., also on the 13th of Dhul Hijja. The Hanafi proof regarding the days of sacrifice is that Abdullah ibn Amr, Ibn Abbas, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) said: 'The days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr) are three, and the best of them is the first.' The manner of reasoning is that since the days of sacrifice are among the quantities of the Shariah, and in quantities opinion does not apply, therefore in determining the days of sacrifice, opinion also does not apply. Since opinion has no role in the days of sacrifice, their determination is dependent on hearing (sam'). He said: 'It is permissible in three days...' his statement is clear. (Al-Hidayah, Book of Udhiyah, vol. 4 p. 449)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the second principle (qa'ida) that personal opinion cannot ascertain the quantities legislated by the Shariah. The author applies this to the days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr). The Hanafi position is that sacrifice is permissible on three days: 10th, 11th, and 12th Dhul Hijja. Imam Shafi'i holds that it is also permissible on the 13th, making four days. The Hanafi proof is the statement of the Companions (Abdullah ibn Amr, Ibn Abbas, Ali) that 'the days of nahr are three, and the best of them is the first,' and they stated this based on hearing (sam'an) rather than opinion. Since the days are among the quantities (maqadir) that cannot be determined by opinion, they must be established by transmission (sam'). The text then quotes Al-Hidayah confirming the permissibility in three days.

Key Terms
مقادير شرع (maqadir shara'): The divinely legislated quantities and measures, such as nisab, fixed periods, and specific numbers, which cannot be altered by human reasoning.
سماع (sam'): Hearing or receiving knowledge directly from authentic sources, i.e., revelation or transmitted reports from the Prophet or Companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed, how are Shariah quantities (maqadir) determined?
A) Through personal opinion (ra'y)
B) Through analogical reasoning (qiyas)
C) Through transmission (sam') from the sources
D) Through scholarly consensus (ijma)

Key Takeaway
Shariah quantities like nisab and days of sacrifice are fixed by transmitted evidence, not human reasoning.

Application: Days of Sacrifice and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Resolving a dispute by applying the principle that Shariah quantities are known by transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the days of sacrifice (10th-12th Dhul Hijja) and how the principle of maqadir supports it against the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Sacrifice is valid on three days only — the Companion report is a textual quantity that blocks extended qiyas.

This lesson applies the principle that Shariah quantities are known by transmission to a specific dispute: the number of days for sacrifice (udhiyah). The Hanafi school holds that sacrifice is permissible on three days (10th-12th Dhul Hijja), while Imam al-Shafi'i adds a fourth day (13th). The Hanafi proof is the statement of several Companions that 'the days of nahr are three', which constitutes a transmitted quantity. The passage illustrates how a qa'ida can settle an inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that sacrifice (udhiyah) is permissible on three days: the 10th of Dhul Hijja (yawm al-nahr) and the 11th and 12th (the two days after).
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sacrifice is also permissible on the 13th of Dhul Hijja, making it four days.
The passage does not detail Shafi'i proof; it only states the difference.
3
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the transmitted report from Abdullah ibn Amr, Ibn Abbas, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) that 'the days of nahr are three, and the best of them is the first.'
This is a sam' (transmission) from Companions.
4
Apply the principle of maqadir
Since the days of sacrifice are among the Shariah quantities (maqadir), they cannot be determined by opinion or qiyas. The companion report provides the quantity; therefore, no addition is allowed.
This is the core of the Hanafi reasoning.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence is that for Hanafis, sacrifice after sunset on the 12th is invalid, while Shafi'is allow it on the 13th.
This affects timing for pilgrims and others.

Source Text

Major and Minor Defects in Sacrificial Animals
Stating the legal maxim distinguishing major and minor defects in sacrificial animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between major and minor defects (ayb fahish and ayb yasir) in sacrificial animals and identify which defects invalidate the sacrifice according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A major defect (most of a limb missing) invalidates sacrifice; a minor defect (most remaining) does not.

In the Hanafi school, not every imperfection in a sacrificial animal prevents its use. The author of Al-Hidayah lays down a clear principle: only defects that are considered 'major' (ayb fahish) invalidate the sacrifice, while minor defects (ayb yasir) are overlooked. This lesson unpacks that distinction with examples, helping you apply this rule when selecting an animal for udhiyah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the maxim
Read the core principle: major defect prevents validity, minor does not. This is the foundational rule.
The maxim is quantitative: 'most of a limb' is the benchmark.
2
Define the criteria
Identify the quantitative criterion: major defect means most of a limb is missing; minor defect means most remains.
This applies to limbs like ears, tail, etc.
3
Apply to given examples
The text provides examples: blind, lame, and one-eyed animals are not permissible. These are major defects.
Note that these are not necessarily about missing limbs but are considered major by analogy.
4
Extend to other defects
Use the same quantitative criterion for other defects like a cut tail or torn ear. If most of the tail/ear is missing, it is major; otherwise minor.
The text begins to discuss the tail but is cut off.
5
Determine the ruling
Once you classify the defect as major or minor, state the ruling: major → sacrifice invalid (batil); minor → valid (sahih).
An animal with any major defect cannot be used; a minor defect is overlooked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْعَيْبُ الْفَاحِشُ يَمْنَعُ عَنْ جَوَازِ التَّضْحِيَةِ وَالْيَسِيرُ غَيْرُ مَانِعِ . ترجمہ: عیب فاحش قربانی کے جواز سے مانع ہے اور عیب یسیر مانع نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر قربانی کے جانور میں عیب فاحش یعنی بڑا عیب ہو تو قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی اور اگر عیب پیر یعنی معمولی سا ہو تو قربانی جائز ہے، عیب فاحش مثلاً کسی عضو کا اکثر حصہ کٹ جانا اور عیب سیسر مثلاً کسی عضو کا اکثر حصہ باقی رہنا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اندھے لنگڑے اور کانے جانور کی قربانی جائز نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اس جانور کی قربانی بھی جائز نہیں ہے جس کی دم کا
The major defect prevents the permissibility of sacrifice, and the minor defect is not preventing. Translation: Major defect prevents the validity of sacrifice, and minor defect does not prevent. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if the sacrificial animal has a major defect, i.e., a big defect, then the sacrifice will not be permissible, and if there is a minor defect, i.e., a slight one, then the sacrifice is permissible. Major defect, for example, most of a limb being cut off, and minor defect, for example, most of a limb remaining. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that a blind, lame, or one-eyed animal's sacrifice is not permissible, similarly the sacrifice of an animal whose tail is [cut off?]... (incomplete).

Commentary
This passage presents a third principle regarding defects in sacrificial animals. The author distinguishes between major defects (ayb fahish) and minor defects (ayb yasir). Major defects, such as the loss of most of a limb, prevent the validity of the sacrifice. Minor defects, where most of the limb remains, do not invalidate. The text then gives examples: a blind, lame, or one-eyed animal is not acceptable, nor is an animal whose tail is mostly cut off. The commentary is cut off at the end.

Key Terms
عييب فاحش (ayb fahish): A major defect in the sacrificial animal that invalidates the sacrifice, e.g., most of a limb missing.
عييب يسير (ayb yasir): A minor defect that does not invalidate the sacrifice, e.g., most of the limb still present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A sacrifice is invalid if the animal has a major defect (most of a limb missing), but valid if the defect is minor (most of the limb intact).

Days of Sacrifice: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Explaining Hanafi position on days of sacrifice and rebutting Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissible days for udhiyah and explain the evidence from the Companions, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Sacrifice is valid only on three days: 10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul-Hijjah — based on Companion statements heard from the Prophet.

When is it valid to perform the udhiyah sacrifice? The Hanafi school gives a precise answer: three specific days. This lesson examines the ruling from al-Hidayah, the proof from the Companions, and the reason why the Hanafis reject extending it to a fourth day, as Imam al-Shafi'i held.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the explicit ruling from the text: sacrifice is valid on the day of Nahr (10th) and the two days after (11th-12th). Note that this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.
The text says 'jā'iz' (permissible) on three days.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sacrifice is also valid on the 13th — three days after the day of Nahr, making a total of four days.
The text does not elaborate on the Shafi'i proof.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the statement of Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas: 'Ayyam al-nahr thalathah' (the days of Nahr are three), which they said based on hearing (sama') from the Prophet.
This is considered a legal measure (miqdar) where personal opinion has no role.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the opponent
The Hanafi response is that the determination of these days is a legal measure (miqdar shar'i), and such measures cannot be extended by analogy or personal opinion; they must be taken as transmitted.
The text says 'al-ra'y lā yuhtadā ilā al-maqādīr' — opinion does not guide to measures.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: for Hanafis, slaughtering on the 13th is invalid and the sacrifice must be repeated; for Shafi'is, it is valid and no repetition is needed.
This affects when Muslims following each school can perform the sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور دو دن بعد میں ، یعنی دس گیارہ، بارہ ذی الحجہ میں جائز ہے، جبکہ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یوم انحر کے تین دن بعد بھی قربانی جائز ہے یعنی تیرویں ذی الحجہ میں بھی۔ احناف کی دلیل ایام قربانی کے بارے میں یہ ہے کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمرو، حضرت ابن عباس اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہم فرماتے ہیں کہ ایام نحر تین دن ہیں اور ان میں افضل پہلا دن ہے، طرز استدلال اس طرح ہے کہ چونکہ ایام قربانی مقادیر شرع میں سے ہے اور مقادیر میں رائے نہیں چلتی، لہذا ایام قربانی کی تعیین میں بھی رائے نہیں چلے گی ، جب ایامِ قربانی میں رائے کا کوئی عمل دخل نہیں ہے تو اس کی تعیین سماع پر موقوف ہوگی۔
قَالَ (وَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ إِلَخُ كَلَامُهُ وَاضِحٌ.
(العناية: كتاب الأضحية، ج ۹ ص ۵۱۳)
وهي جائزة في ثلاثة أيام) وهى يوم النحر، ويومان بعده)، لما روى عن عمر وعلى وابن عباس رضي الله عنهم، قالوا: أيام النحر ثلاثة أفضلها أولها، وقد قالوه سماعا لأن الرأى لا يهتدى إلى المقادير
اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الأضحية، ج ۳ ص ۲۳٤)
الهداية كتاب الأضحية، ج ٤ ص ٤٤٩
It is permissible on three days: the day of Nahr and two days after. Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) says that sacrifice is also permissible three days after the day of Nahr, i.e., on the 13th of Dhul-Hijjah. The Hanafi evidence regarding the days of sacrifice is that Abdullah ibn Amr, Ibn Abbas, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) said: the days of Nahr are three, the best of them is the first. The method of reasoning is that since the days of sacrifice are among the legal measures (maqadir shar'iyyah) and personal opinion does not operate in measures, therefore personal opinion does not operate in determining the days of sacrifice. When personal opinion has no role in the days of sacrifice, then its determination is based on hearing (sama'). He said: (It is permissible in three days...) his words are clear. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 9 p. 513) (It is permissible in three days) i.e., the day of Nahr and two days after, based on what has been narrated from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). They said: the days of Nahr are three, the best of them is the first, and they said it based on hearing because personal opinion does not guide to the measures. (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 3 p. 234) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 4 p. 449)
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the number of days for udhiyah (sacrificial slaughter). The Hanafi position, stated by al-Quduri and expanded by the commentator, is that sacrifice is valid only on three days: the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr) and the two following days (11th and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it extends to a fourth day (the 13th). The Hanafi proof relies on reports from Companions (Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas) who explicitly limit the days to three, emphasizing that this is a purely legal measure (miqdar shar'i) where human reasoning (ra'y) has no authority. The commentator notes that since such measures cannot be reached by analogy or opinion, they must be determined by transmitted reports (sama'). Thus, the Hanafi school adheres strictly to the three-day limit.

Key Terms
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrificial slaughter; specifically three days: 10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul-Hijjah according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on how many days is the sacrifice of an animal valid during Dhul-Hijjah?
A) Two days
B) Three days
C) Four days
D) Seven days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits udhiyah to three specific days based on Companion statements that are considered direct legal measures, rejecting any extension by opinion.

Major vs Minor Defects in Sacrificial Animals
Stating the principle with examples and rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between major and minor defects in sacrificial animals and apply the Hanafi ruling that major defects invalidate sacrifice while minor ones do not.

Core Idea
A major defect invalidates sacrifice; a minor defect is overlooked for practicality.

This lesson examines the Hanafi principle regarding defects in sacrificial animals (udhiyah). Not every imperfection renders the sacrifice invalid; only major defects that significantly affect the animal or its meat do. The author of al-Hidayah provides the rule and examples, along with the rationale that animals are rarely free from minor defects, so strictness would cause hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Locate the rule stated in the text: 'Major defect prevents the permissibility of sacrifice and minor does not prevent.' This is the foundational principle.
The principle is expressed in both Arabic and Urdu translation.
2
List the examples of major defects
The author mentions specific defects: blind (al-'amya'), one-eyed (al-'awra'), lame that cannot walk to the slaughter place, emaciated (al-'ajfa'), and loss of most of the tail or ear. These are all major defects.
Other schools may have slightly different lists.
3
Understand the criterion for minor defects
Minor defects are defined as those that have no effect on the meat and are common. The text states: 'the minor is that which has no effect on its meat.'
Commonness is key: animals are rarely free from minor defects, so ignoring them prevents hardship.
4
Analyze the rationale (ta'lil)
The rationale given: 'an animal is rarely free from a minor defect.' This shows the principle is based on ease and practicality, not on a strict textual proof.
The ruling is derived from general principles and the practice of the Companions (Qawl Sahabi), though no specific hadith is cited.
5
Note the authority level
The text quotes al-Hidayah and al-'Inayah, both from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus, so the ruling is authoritative within the Hanafi school.
Intra-Hanafi differences are minimal on this point.

(24) Major defect prevents the permissibility of sacrifice and minor does not prevent. Translation: Major defect prevents the permissibility of sacrifice and minor defect does not prevent. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if the sacrificial animal has a major defect (big defect) then the sacrifice is not valid, and if it has a minor defect (small) then the sacrifice is valid. Major defect example: most of a limb being cut off; minor defect example: most of a limb remaining. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, states that a blind, lame, or one-eyed animal is not valid for sacrifice; similarly, an animal whose most of the tail or most of the ear has been cut off is not valid, because these are major defects and major defects prevent the validity of sacrifice. However, if there is a minor defect, the sacrifice is valid, because few animals are free from minor defects and such defects do not affect the meat. He said: It is not permissible to sacrifice a blind (animal) or a one-eyed (animal). This is a statement of what is not permissible to sacrifice. The principle in this is that major defect prevents and minor does not prevent, because an animal is rarely free from a minor defect, and minor is that which has no effect on its meat. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 9 p. 514) He said: It is not permissible to sacrifice a blind (animal) – that is, al-Quduri said... and (a one-eyed) which has lost one eye, (and a lame which cannot walk to the slaughter place) – with fatha on the meem and sukoon on the seen? Actually 'al-mansak' with fatha on meem and sukoon on noon? – and it is the place where it is slaughtered, and the qiyas in it is fatha? ... (and a thin/emaciated) i.e., emaciated. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 12 p. 33) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 4 p. 449)
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage explains a key ruling regarding defects in sacrificial animals. The principle is that a major defect (al-'ayb al-fahish) prevents the sacrifice from being valid, while a minor defect (al-'ayb al-yasir) does not. The author provides examples: major defects include blindness, lameness, one-eyedness, or the loss of most of the tail or ear. Minor defects are those where the majority of the limb remains, and such defects are common and do not affect the meat quality. The rationale (ta'lil) is that animals are seldom free from minor defects, and such defects do not impact the flesh, so they are overlooked in the interest of ease. The text also quotes the principle from al-Hidayah and al-'Inayah, and lists specific animals that are not valid, such as the blind (al-'amya'), one-eyed (al-'awra'), lame, and emaciated (al-'ajfa'). These rulings are based on the general rule that major defects invalidate the sacrifice.

Key Terms
العيب الفاحش (al-'ayb al-fahish): A major defect in the sacrificial animal that prevents the validity of sacrifice, e.g., loss of most of a limb or organ.
العيب اليسير (al-'ayb al-yasir): A minor defect that does not prevent the validity of sacrifice, e.g., most of the limb remaining and no effect on meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It affects the meat
B) It is rare
C) It has no effect on the meat and is common
D) It makes the animal unusable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sacrifice with minor defects due to their commonness and lack of effect on meat, but prohibits sacrifice with major defects.

6 min
State of Slaughter and Its Preliminaries
Stating a principle of attachment of slaughter preliminaries to slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding defects occurring during the slaughter process and apply it to the case of a broken leg.

Core Idea
Accidental defects during slaughter do not invalidate the sacrifice by istihsan.

In Hanafi fiqh, the rulings of slaughter are extended to its preliminaries. This principle provides leniency: if an animal suffers a defect while being prepared for slaughter, the sacrifice remains valid by istihsan. Let us examine the principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The text states: 'The state of slaughter and its preliminaries are attached to slaughter.' This means any happening during the act and its preparations is legally considered part of the slaughter.
2
Understand the example
The example given: an animal's leg breaks while being taken to slaughter or while being laid down. This is a defect that would normally invalidate a sacrifice, but here it is overlooked.
3
Apply istihsan reasoning
Istihsan (juristic preference) is used to avoid hardship. Since the defect occurred during the process of slaughter, the sacrifice is considered valid by virtue of this principle.
4
Examine the consequence
The ruling: the sacrifice is valid (sahih) by istihsan. The defect does not break the validity because it is attached to the slaughter act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۵) حَالَةُ الذَّبْحِ وَمُقَدَّمَاتُهُ مُلْحِقَةٌ بالأبح.
ترجمہ: ذبح کی حالت اور اس کے مقدمات ذبح کے ساتھ ملحق ہوتے ہیں۔ تشریح مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جانور کو ذبح کرنے کی حالت اور اس کے مقدمات یعنی اسباب ذبح کے ساتھ ملحق ہوں گے، یعنی ذبح میں جو احکام مرتب ہوں گے وہی احکام اسباب ذبح کے بھی ہوں گے، مثلاً جانور کو نذبح تک لے جانے کے وقت ٹانگ وغیرہ کا ٹوٹ جانا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر قربانی کے جانور کو ذبح کرنے کے لئے لٹایا اور گراتے وقت اس کا پاؤں ٹوٹ گیا اور پھر ذبح کیا تو یہ استحسانا جائز
(25) The state of slaughter and its preliminaries are attached to slaughter. Translation: The state of slaughter and its preliminaries are attached to slaughter. Explanation: The meaning of the said principle is that the state of slaughtering the animal and its preliminaries, i.e., the causes of slaughter, will be attached to the slaughter; that is, the rulings that apply to slaughter will also apply to the causes of slaughter. For example, if the animal's leg breaks while being taken to slaughter, or if when laying it down for slaughter its foot breaks, and then it is slaughtered, then by istihsan it is permissible.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage presents another principle related to sacrificial animals: the state of slaughter (halat al-dhabh) and its preliminaries (muqaddimat) are attached to the slaughter itself. This means that any accident that occurs during the process leading up to slaughter, such as breaking a leg while bringing the animal to the slaughter place or while positioning it, does not invalidate the sacrifice. By istihsan (juristic preference), the sacrifice remains valid because these incidents are considered part of the slaughter act. This is a leniency from the Hanafi school to avoid hardship for the owner. The text cites the example of a leg breaking when laying the animal down; such a defect would normally be major, but since it occurs during the process, it is overlooked.

Key Terms
حالة الذبح (halat al-dhabh): The actual act of slaughtering the animal.
مقدمات الذبح (muqaddimat al-dhabh): The preliminaries of slaughter, such as bringing the animal, positioning it, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sacrifice is invalid because the animal became defective
B) The sacrifice is valid by istihsan because the defect occurred during the slaughter process
C) The sacrifice is valid only if the leg is repaired
D) The sacrifice is invalid regardless of when the defect occurred

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that the state of slaughter and its preliminaries are attached to slaughter ensures that accidental defects during the process do not invalidate the sacrifice, by istihsan.

Preliminaries of Slaughter Are Annexed to Slaughter
Explaining annexation of slaughter preliminaries via an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that preliminaries of slaughter are annexed to the act, and distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in a case of defect during preparation.

Core Idea
Preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter; a defect during preparation does not invalidate the sacrifice by istihsan.

Imagine you have designated a sheep for Eid sacrifice. As you lay it down, it struggles and breaks its leg. Is your sacrifice still valid? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on such a case, where the principle that the state of slaughter and its preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter itself resolves the issue by istihsan, overriding qiyas. We will also examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the role of immediacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle and its scope
Read the principle: 'The state of slaughter and its preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter.' Understand that this means any defect occurring during the acts of preparing the animal for slaughter (like laying it down, bringing it to the place) is legally treated as if it occurred during the slaughter itself.
The principle is a form of istihsan that eases the obligation of sacrifice.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the broken leg case
Identify the positions: Imam Muhammad holds the sacrifice valid by istihsan. Abu Yusuf holds it invalid if the immediacy (fawr) between laying down and slaughter is interrupted. Trace the proofs: Muhammad's proof is that the defect happened by the preliminaries; Abu Yusuf's proof is qiyas that the obligation is fulfilled by slaughter, not laying down, and interruption severs the causal link.
The dispute hinges on whether the preliminaries are fully annexed regardless of a time gap.
3
Contrast with the majority Hanafi position and opposing schools
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is Imam Muhammad's view. Zufar and al-Shafi'i agree with Abu Yusuf in invalidating. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis (mufta bihi) validate the sacrifice; Shafi'is do not.
This illustrates how usul principles (istihsan vs qiyas) produce different fiqh rulings.
4
Relate to the general rule on serious vs minor defects
The passage also notes that serious defects (al-ayb al-fahish) prevent sacrifice entirely, while minor defects do not. The broken leg is a serious defect, but because it occurred during the preliminaries, it is annexed and thus does not invalidate in the Hanafi view.
The annexation principle overrides the general prohibition of sacrificing a defective animal.

Source Text

اصول ہدایہ راج
۲۱۷
ہے، کیونکہ جانور کولٹانا اور مذبح وغیرہ تک پہنچانا اسباب ذبح میں سے ہے اور اسباب ذبح، ذبح کے ساتھ ملحق ہوتے ہیں، لہذا یہ لٹانا بھی ذبح کے ساتھ ملحق ہوگا اور جب ذبح کے وقت پاؤں وغیرہ ٹوٹ جائے تو قربانی جائز ہوتی ہے، لہذا ذبح کے لئے لٹانے کے وقت بھی اگر پاؤں ٹوٹ گیا تو قربانی جائز ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر کوئی جانور لٹانے کے بعد برک کر بھاگ گیا اور اس میں کوئی عیب پیدا ہو گیا، لیکن فوراً اسے پکڑ کر ذبح کر دیا گیا تو اس کی قربانی درست ہے، اس لیے کہ یہ صورت بھی مقدمات ذبیح کی ہے، لہذا اسے بھی ذبیح کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جائے گا۔
(۲۲) حُكْمُ الْبَدْلِ حُكْمُ الْمُبْدَلِ .
ترجمہ: بدل کا حکم مبدل کا حکم ہوتا ہے۔
وَقَوْلُهُ فَانْكَسَرَتْ رِجُلُهَا ..... فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا أَصَابَهَا مَانِعٌ غَيْرُ الْانْكِسَارِ بِالاضْطِرَابِ حَالَةَ الْإِضْجَاعِ لِلدَّبْحِ كَانَ الْحُكْمُ كَذَلِكَ، وَإِنَّمَا قُيِّدَ الْإِجْزَاءُ بِالِاسْتِحْسَانِ لِأَنَّ وَجْهَ الْقِيَاسِ بِخِلَافِهِ، لأَنَّ تَأْدِى الْوَاجِبِ بِالتَّضْحِيَةِ لَا بِالْإِضْجَاعِ وَهِيَ مَعِيبَةٌ عِنْدَهَا فَصَارَ كَمَا لَوْ كَانَتْ كَذَلِكَ قَبْلَهُ. وَقَوْلُهُ لأَنَّهُ حَصَلَ بِمُقَدِّمَاتِ الذَّبْحِ) دَلِيلُ مُحَمَّدٍ. وَدَلِيلُ أَبِى يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ أَنَّ الْفَوْرَ لَمَّا انْقَطَعَ خَرَجَ الْفِعْلُ الَّذِي تَعَيَّنَتْ بِهِ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ سَبَبًا مِنْ أَسْبَابِ هَذَا الذَّبْحِ الَّذِي وُجِدَ بَعْدَ الْفَوْرِ فَصَارَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ مَا حَصَلَ بِفِعْلٍ آخَرَ . (العناية: كتاب الأضحية، ج ۹ ص ۵۱۶) (ولو أضجعها) أى ولو أضجع رجل شاته التي عينها للتضحية. فاضطربت فانكسرت رجلها فذبحها أجزأه استحسانا عندنا، خلافا لزفر والشافعي رحمهما الله...... ( لأن حالة الذبح ومقدماته ملحقة بالذبح) وهذا إشارة على وجه الاستحسان البناية: كتاب الأضحية، ج ۱۲ ص ۴۴)

Principles of Hidayah, volume 4. Most of the part or most of the ear has been cut off, because these are serious defects and a serious defect prevents the validity of sacrifice, so these defects also prevent validity, and such an animal's sacrifice is not valid. However, if it is a minor defect, sacrifice is valid, because few animals are free from minor defects and it has no effect on the meat. (25) The state of slaughter and its preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter. Translation: The state of slaughter and its preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the state of slaughtering the animal and its preliminaries, i.e., the causes of slaughter, will be annexed to the slaughter, meaning that the rulings that apply to the slaughter will also apply to the causes of slaughter. For example, breaking of the leg while taking the animal to be slaughtered. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to state that if the sacrificial animal is laid down for slaughter and its leg breaks while being laid down, and then it is slaughtered, it is valid by istihsan. He said: And one does not sacrifice a blind animal, nor a one-eyed animal. This is a clarification of what is not permissible to sacrifice. The principle in this is that a serious defect prevents, while a minor one does not, because an animal is rarely free from minor defects, and a minor defect is that which has no effect on its meat. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Udhiya, vol. 9, p. 514) He said: And one does not sacrifice a blind animal, i.e., al-Quduri said... and a one-eyed animal, i.e., that which has one eye missing, and a lame animal that cannot walk to the place of sacrifice, with a fatha on the mim and sukun on the sin without kasra, which is the place where it is slaughtered, and the analogy is to open it from نسك for Allah a نسكا and منسكا if he slaughters for His sake... and not an emaciated animal, i.e., the thin one. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Udhiya, vol. 12, p. 33) Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Udhiya, vol. 4, p. 449. Principles of Hidayah, page 217. Because laying down the animal and bringing it to the place of slaughter are among the causes of slaughter, and the causes of slaughter are annexed to the slaughter. So this laying down is also annexed to the slaughter, and when the leg breaks at the time of slaughter, the sacrifice is valid. Therefore, if the leg breaks while laying down for slaughter, the sacrifice is valid. Similarly, if an animal after being laid down jumps and runs away and develops a defect, but it is immediately caught and slaughtered, its sacrifice is valid, because this situation is also among the preliminaries of slaughter, so it will be annexed to the slaughter. (22) The ruling of the substitute is the ruling of the substituted. Translation: The ruling of the substitute is the ruling of the substituted. And his statement: then its leg broke... if a preventing factor other than breakage occurs due to agitation during the state of laying down for slaughter, the ruling is the same. Permission is restricted to istihsan because the analogy is contrary, since the fulfillment of the obligation is by sacrifice, not by laying down, and it is defective at that time, so it becomes as if it was like that before. And his statement: because it occurred by the preliminaries of slaughter is the proof of Muhammad. And the proof of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) is that when the immediacy was interrupted, the act by which it was designated ceased to be a cause of this slaughter that occurred after the interruption, so it became like something that occurred by another act. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Udhiya, vol. 9, p. 516) (And if he laid it down) i.e., if a man laid down his sheep that he had designated for sacrifice, and it became agitated and its leg broke, and he slaughtered it, it is valid by istihsan according to us, contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them)... (because the state of slaughter and its preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter) and this indicates the basis of istihsan. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Udhiya, vol. 12, p. 44) Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Udhiya, vol. 4, p. 450.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses two related principles concerning the sacrifice (udhiya). The first principle (25) states that the state of slaughter and its preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter itself, meaning that acts performed in preparation for slaughter are legally treated as part of the slaughter. The second principle (22) states that the ruling of a substitute is the ruling of the substituted. The main focus is a case: a person designates a sheep for sacrifice, lays it down to slaughter it, but the sheep becomes agitated and breaks its leg before the slaughter actually takes place. According to istihsan (juristic preference), the sacrifice is valid because the injury occurred during the preliminaries of slaughter, which are annexed to the slaughter itself. This is the view of Imam Muhammad. Abu Yusuf, however, argues that if there is a break in immediacy (fawr) between the laying down and the slaughter, the act of laying down is no longer a cause of that slaughter, so it becomes like a defect occurring before the designation. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the breaking occurred by the preliminaries of slaughter, so it is attached. The Hanafi school follows Imam Muhammad's view (istihsan), while Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that such a defect invalidates the sacrifice because the animal became defective before the actual slaughter. The passage also clarifies the general rule: serious defects (al-ayb al-fahish) prevent sacrifice, while minor defects (al-yasir) do not, because animals are rarely free from minor defects.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A method of juristic preference where a ruling is adopted based on equity, custom, or public interest, overriding qiyas.
مقدمات الذبح (muqaddimat al-dhabh): The preliminary acts necessary for slaughter, such as laying the animal down, sharpening the knife, and bringing it to the slaughter place.
العيب الفاحش (al-ayb al-fahish): A serious defect that significantly detracts from the animal's value or health, such as blindness, loss of an ear, or lameness that prevents walking.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the requirement that the slaughter follow the preparatory acts without significant delay. Abu Yusuf considers interruption of fawr as severing the legal connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proof of Imam Muhammad for validating the sacrifice when the leg breaks during laying down?
A) The animal was not yet defective at the time of designation.
B) The defect occurred by the preliminaries of slaughter, which are annexed to the slaughter.
C) The hadith permits sacrifice of any animal that was healthy at purchase.
D) The sacrifice is a religious duty and must be performed regardless.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that preliminaries are annexed to the slaughter means a defect during preparation (e.g., breaking a leg while laying down) does not invalidate the sacrifice by istihsan, following Imam Muhammad's view.

Ruling on a Sacrificial Animal Breaking Its Leg During Laying Down
Explains Hanafi istihsan ruling on broken leg during laying down for sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sacrificial animal that breaks its leg during laying down and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
A defect during the preliminaries of slaughter is excused by istihsan, making the sacrifice valid.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case from the Hanafi school: an animal designated for sacrifice breaks its leg while being laid down for slaughter. While qiyas would suggest the sacrifice is invalid due to the defect, the Hanafi school applies istihsan to validate it. We will explore the reasoning behind this, the intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, and the practical implications for sacrificial practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The case: a person designates a sheep for sacrifice, lays it down, and in its agitation it breaks its leg. Is the sacrifice valid?
2
State the qiyas ruling
By qiyas, the sacrifice would be invalid because the obligation is to sacrifice a sound animal, and this animal is defective at the time of slaughter.
This is the position of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.
3
State the istihsan ruling
The Hanafi school rules the sacrifice valid by istihsan, because the injury occurred during the preliminaries of slaughter, which are attached to the slaughter itself.
The preliminaries include laying down and bringing to the slaughter place.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds validity unconditionally. Imam Abu Yusuf restricts validity to cases where there is no break in immediacy (fawr) between the injury and slaughter.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view, validating the sacrifice.
5
Apply the ruling to a related scenario
If the animal runs away after being laid down and acquires a defect, but is immediately caught and slaughtered, the sacrifice is also valid.
This is because the escape and defect still occur within the preliminaries.

Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. It discusses the case where an animal designated for sacrifice breaks its leg while being laid down for slaughter. The Hanafi school, by istihsan, considers the sacrifice valid, contrary to qiyas which would require an unblemished animal at the time of slaughter. The reason for istihsan is that the actions leading up to slaughter (such as laying down) are considered attached to the slaughter itself, so any defect occurring during these preliminaries is overlooked. Imam Muhammad argues that because the injury happened during the preliminaries, it is treated as part of the slaughter. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, argues that if there is a break in immediacy (fawr) between the injury and slaughter, then the injury is no longer connected to the slaughter and thus invalidates the sacrifice. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that the sacrifice is valid by istihsan, as stated in the text. The passage also notes that the ruling is contrary to the positions of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who would consider such an animal invalid.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A legal method preferring a different ruling over qiyas due to a stronger evidence or necessity; here, it validates the sacrifice despite the defect.
مقدمات الذبح (muqaddimat al-dhabh): The preliminary acts leading up to slaughter, such as laying down the animal and bringing it to the slaughter place, which are considered attached to the slaughter.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the condition of acting without delay. Here, Abu Yusuf argues that if there is a break in immediacy between the injury and slaughter, the connection is lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The sacrifice is invalid because the animal is defective.
B) The sacrifice is valid by istihsan because the injury occurred during the preliminaries of slaughter.
C) The sacrifice is valid only if the owner did not cause the injury.
D) The sacrifice is invalid unless the animal is immediately slaughtered after the injury.

Key Takeaway
A sacrificial animal that develops a defect during the preliminaries of slaughter is considered valid by istihsan, because the preliminaries are attached to the slaughter itself.

The Ruling of the Substitute is the Ruling of the Substituend
States and explains a legal maxim with application to sacrificial skin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim 'Hukm al-badl hukm al-mubdal', explain its application to the skin of a sacrificial animal, and distinguish between permissible and impermissible substitutes based on durability.

Core Idea
The substitute inherits the same ruling as the original in all matters, unless a specific prohibition exists.

This lesson introduces a fundamental legal maxim that governs many transactions in Hanafi fiqh: the substitute takes the same ruling as the original. The author of Al-Hidayah illustrates this maxim with the case of the skin of a sacrificial animal, showing that using the skin itself is permissible, and therefore using its price to buy durable goods is also permissible by istihsan. However, if the substitute is consumable, the ruling changes because the benefit is not ongoing.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Begin by memorizing the Arabic wording: حُكْمُ الْبَدْلِ حُكْمُ الْمُبْدَلِ. Understand that 'badl' is the substitute and 'mubdal' is the original. The substitute is like a deputy (na'ib) and carries the same ruling as the original.
This is a general principle in mu'amalat.
2
Apply the maxim to the skin of a sacrificial animal
The original item (mubdal) is the skin. Since benefiting from the skin is permissible (e.g., making a prayer mat), the substitute (badl) – whether a purchased item or the price – also becomes permissible as long as the benefit is ongoing (intifa' bi-baqa' al-'ayn).
The ruling is by istihsan, not strict qiyas.
3
Distinguish between durable and consumable substitutes
If the substitute is a durable good like a mat or bag, its use is permissible because it remains intact. If it is a consumable like vinegar or dirhams, it is not permissible because the benefit involves consumption (itlaf), which is akin to selling the skin for money, which is prohibited.
The key condition is baqa' al-'ayn (continuation of substance).
4
Identify the basis of istihsan
The permissibility is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid hardship. While the skin itself is permissible to use, selling it for dirhams would be strictly prohibited. However, buying durable goods with the price is allowed by istihsan, respecting the maxim.
The maxim itself is a tool for istihsan in this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲) حُكْمُ الْبَدْلِ حُكْمُ الْمُبْدَلِ . )
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مبدل کا جو حکم ہوتا ہے وہی حکم بدل کا بھی ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ بدل نائب ہے اور مبدل اصل ہے اور اصل اور نائب حکم میں مخالف نہیں ہوتے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا ر ہے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی شخص مین کو اپنے استعمال میں لائے، مثلاً کھال سے مصلی ، دستر خوان ، ڈول یا تھیلا وغیرہ بنا کر اپنے استعمال میں لائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں، اگر چہ افضل یہ ہے کہ صدقہ کرے۔ جب گوشت سے نفع حاصل کرنا جائز ہے تو کھال جو گوشت سے کم درجے کی ہے، اس سے تو بدرجہ اولیٰ انتفاع درست ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر قربانی کی کھال بیچ کر کسی نے کوئی ایسی چیز خرید لی کہ جب تک وہ چیز باقی رہے گی انتفاع ہوتا رہے گا، مثلا مصلی ، دستر خوان وغیرہ تو یہ بھی بطور استحسان درست ہے، اس لیے کہ بدل اور مبدل دونوں کا حکم ایک ہوتا ہے، جب عین مبدل یعنی کھال سے انتفاع درست ہے، تو اس کے بدل یعنی اس سے خریدی ہوئی چیز سے بھی انتفاع درست ہوگا۔ اور اگر کھال کے عوض ایسی چیز خریدی جس سے بقائے عین کے ساتھ انتفاع ناممکن ہو، مثلاً سرکہ وغیرہ استعمال سے یہ خود ہی نا پید ہو جاتے ہیں اور انہیں ہلاک کر کے ہی ان سے انتفاع ہوسکتا ہے، تو اس صورت میں یہ بیچ درست نہ ہوگی اور نہ ہی ان چیزوں سے انتفاع درست ہوگا، جیسا کہ اگر در اہم کے عوض کھال فروخت کر دی تو یہ بیج جائز نہیں ہے۔
ولا بأس بأن يشترى به ما ينتفع بعينه في البيت مع بقائه استحسانا) أي لا بأس بأن يشترى بجلد الأضحية الذي ينتفع بعينه مع بقاء عينه كالجرب والغربال...... وذلك مثل ما ذكرنا أى الذى ينتفع بعينه مع بقائه مثل النطع والجراب ونحوهما لأن للبدل حكم المبدل) المبدل هو الجلد الذي يشترى به لما كان البدل من الحكم فهو للمبدل كذلك (البناية: كتاب الأضحية، ج ۱۲ ص ۵۴)
(22) The ruling of the substitute is the ruling of the substituend.
Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the ruling of the substituend (mubdal) is the same as the ruling of the substitute (badl), because the substitute is a deputy and the substituend is the original, and the original and its deputy are not opposed in ruling. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a person uses a mat for his own use, for example, making a prayer mat, tablecloth, bucket, or bag from the skin and uses it, there is no harm, although it is better to give it in charity. When benefiting from meat is permissible, then benefiting from the skin, which is of a lower grade than meat, is even more appropriate. Similarly, if one sells the skin of the sacrificial animal and buys something that will continue to provide benefit as long as it remains, such as a prayer mat or tablecloth, this is also valid by way of istihsan, because the ruling of the substitute and the substituend is the same. When benefiting from the substituend itself (the skin) is valid, then benefiting from its substitute (the purchased item) will also be valid. But if one buys with the skin something from which benefiting with the continuation of its substance is impossible, such as vinegar etc., which are consumed and disappear upon use, then this sale is not valid, nor is benefiting from those things valid, just as if the skin were sold for dirhams, such a sale is not valid. And there is no harm in buying with it something from which benefit is taken with its substance remaining in the house, by istihsan. That is, there is no harm in buying with the skin of the sacrificial animal something that is benefited from with its substance remaining, like a sieve or a dustpan... and that is like what we mentioned, i.e., something benefited from with its substance remaining, such as a mat or a bag and the like, because the substitute has the ruling of the substituend. The substituend is the skin with which it is bought; since the substitute has the ruling, it is thus the same for the substituend. (Al-Binayah: Kitab al-Udhiyah, vol. 12, p. 54)
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage defines a legal maxim and applies it to the use of the skin of a sacrificial animal. The maxim 'Hukm al-badl hukm al-mubdal' means that the substitute (badl) takes the same ruling as the original item (mubdal). The text explains that it is permissible to use the skin of a sacrificial animal for durable goods like prayer mats or bags, and even to sell the skin and buy such durable items, because the substitute (the purchased item) inherits the ruling of the substituend (the skin), which itself is permissible to use. However, if the skin is sold for something consumable like vinegar or dirhams, it is not allowed, because the benefit from such items is not ongoing (they are consumed or spent). The ruling is based on istihsan, allowing flexibility. The maxim is a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh for understanding substitutions in transactions.

Key Terms
البدل (al-badl): The substitute; something that takes the place of another item, such as the price or purchased item in exchange for the skin.
المبدل (al-mubdal): The substituend; the original item that is being substituted, here the skin of the sacrificial animal.
الانتفاع بقاء العين (al-intifa' bi-baqa' al-'ayn): Benefiting from an item while its substance remains intact, such as using a mat or bag, as opposed to consumables like vinegar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim 'Hukm al-badl hukm al-mubdal', what is the ruling on using the price of the skin of a sacrificial animal to buy a prayer mat?
A) Not permissible because the skin must be given in charity.
B) Permissible by istihsan because the substitute (prayer mat) takes the same ruling as the substituend (skin), which is permissible to use.
C) Permissible only if the prayer mat is also used for charity.
D) Not permissible because the price is like money and cannot be used.

Key Takeaway
The substitute inherits the same ruling as the original in Hanafi fiqh, but only when the substitute provides ongoing benefit (baqa' al-'ayn).

Imitating Polytheists in Appearance is Prohibited
Stating the principle and applying it to gold/silver vessels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that using gold and silver vessels is haram and identify the proof from the hadith and the principle of imitating polytheists.

Core Idea
Imitating polytheists is haram; using gold/silver vessels is a form of that imitation and thus haram.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi principle: imitating polytheists in appearance is prohibited. The specific application discussed in Al-Hidayah is the use of gold and silver vessels for eating, drinking, and other purposes. The ruling is based on the hadith 'Whoever imitates a people is one of them,' and is confirmed across multiple Hanafi sources. Understanding this principle helps you see how general textual evidence is applied to specific everyday practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, determine what act is being ruled upon. The text states that using gold and silver vessels for eating, drinking, applying oil, perfuming, etc., is not permissible. The ruling is explicitly given as 'haram' (prohibited).
The act includes any customary use of the vessel as intended.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence is the hadith 'Whoever imitates a people is one of them' (Sunan Abi Dawud). Additionally, another hadith is cited: 'The one who drinks from a gold or silver vessel is only gurgling Hellfire into his belly.'
Both hadiths are ahad (single narration) but their meaning is considered clear (qati al-dalalah).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The hadith 'Whoever imitates a people is one of them' is general and includes imitating the appearance, customs, and practices of polytheists. Using gold and silver vessels is a specific practice associated with polytheists (as stated in the text), so it falls under this prohibition. The second hadith directly threatens Hellfire, reinforcing the severity.
The Hanafi principle 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub' (a general command indicates obligation) applies to prohibitions as well: a general prohibition indicates haram.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
The prohibition applies to all types of use for both men and women: eating, drinking, applying oil, perfuming, using spoons, kohl sticks, mirrors, pens, inkwells, etc. However, if the item is not used in its customary manner (e.g., purely for decoration), there is no dislike (karahah).
The exception is based on the principle that rulings follow the common customary usage (urf).
5
Confirm the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The mufta bihi is that it is absolutely haram to use gold and silver vessels for any intended purpose. This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon by all schools (muttafaq alayh).
Later Hanafi sources like Al-Lubab confirm this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۱۹
كتاب الكراهية
(۲۷) المُشَبَّهُ بِزِي الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَرَامٌ .
ترجمہ: مشرکین کی ہیئت کی مشابہت اختیار کرنا حرام ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مسلمانوں کے لئے مشرکین کی روش اور طریقہ اقوال و افعال میں اختیار کرنا حرام ہے، کیونکہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد گرامی ہے : وَمَنْ تَشَبَّهَ بِقَوْمٍ فَهُوَ مِنْهُمْ “ جوکسی قوم کے ساتھ مشابہت اختیار کرے گاوہ انہی
میں سے ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ اقتلا ر ہے ہیں کہ سونے اور چاندی کے برتن میں کھانا، پینا، تیل لگانا، خوشبو لگانا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ سونے کے برتن میں کھانا پینا وغیرہ یہ مشرکین کی عادت اور روش ہے، اور مشرکین کی روش اور عادت کی مشابہت اختیار کرنا حرام

الهداية كتاب الكراهية، ج ۴ ص ۴۵۳
سنن أبى داود كتاب اللباس، باب في لبس الشهرة، رقم الحديث: ۴۰۳۱ قال : ولا يجوز الأكل والشرب والادهان والتطيب في آنية الذهب والفضة للرجال)...... لقوله عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ في الذى يشرب في إناء الذهب والفضة:
إنما يجرجر في بطنه نار جهنم . (البناية كتاب الكراهية، ج ۱۲ ص ۶) ولا يجوز الأكل والشرب والأدهان والتطيب وجميع أنواع الاستعمال (في آنية الذهب والفضة للرجال والنساء ) لعموم النص، وكذا الأكل بملعقة ذهب وفضة، والاكتحال بميلهما، وما أشبه ذلك من الاستعمال، كمكحلة ومرآة و قلم و دواة ونحوها ، يعنى إذا استعملت ابتداء فيما صنعت له بحسب متعارف الناس، وإلا فلا كراهة. (اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الكراهية، ج ۴ ص ۱۵۹)
Book of Disliked Acts. (27) Imitating the appearance of polytheists is prohibited. Translation: Adopting the appearance of polytheists is haram. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that it is haram for Muslims to adopt the way and method of polytheists in statements and actions, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever imitates a people is one of them." The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the above principle, states that eating, drinking, applying oil, and perfuming in gold and silver vessels is not permissible, because eating and drinking in gold vessels is the habit and practice of polytheists, and imitating the practice and habit of polytheists is haram. Therefore, eating and drinking in gold vessels is also haram.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage introduces a principle from the Hanafi school: imitating the appearance (zi) of polytheists is haram. The principle is based on the hadith: 'Whoever imitates a people is one of them' (Sunan Abi Dawud). The application here is to gold and silver vessels. The author of Al-Hidayah rules that using gold and silver vessels for eating, drinking, applying oil, perfuming, and all forms of use is prohibited for both men and women. The prohibition extends to using spoons, kohl sticks, mirrors, pens, inkwells, etc., if they are made of gold or silver and are used in the customary manner. If they are not used as originally intended (e.g., as decoration), there is no dislike. The ruling is general for all types of use because the text (hadith) is general. The source for the hadith is Sunan Abi Dawud, and the commentary quotes Al-Binayah and Al-Lubab.

Key Terms
مشابہت (mushabahah): Imitating or resembling the appearance, habits, or practices of polytheists.
كراهية (karahiyah): Literally 'disliked acts'; here it refers to a book of fiqh covering prohibited and disliked matters, often including impermissible acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered haram?
A) Eating from a ceramic plate that has a gold trim.
B) Using a silver spoon to eat soup.
C) Keeping a gold cup as decoration in a display cabinet.
D) Drinking from a wooden cup.

Key Takeaway
Using gold and silver vessels for customary purposes is haram because it imitates polytheists, as proven by the hadith 'Whoever imitates a people is one of them.'
