The Maxim 'La Mu'tabara Bil-Tawabi'' (Subordinates Have No Legal Effect)
Explains the Hanafi maxim and its application to gold/silver plating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'La mu'tabara bil-tawabi'', explain its meaning, and apply it to determine the permissibility of using items with subordinate prohibited substances.

Core Idea
A subordinate (tabi') does not carry an independent ruling; the principal object governs.

Islamic law often deals with composite objects where a prohibited substance is attached to a permissible one. How do we rule? The Hanafi school provides a clear maxim: 'La mu'tabara bil-tawabi'' (subordinates are not considered). This lesson unpacks this principle using the example of gold- or silver-plated vessels and saddles, showing how the ruling follows the principal object, not the subordinate attachment.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Maxim and Its Terminology
First, grasp the definition of 'tabi'' (subordinate) and 'mu'tabar' (considered legally). The maxim means that when a prohibited substance is merely attached as a subordinate to a permissible object, the ruling attaches to the principal, not the subordinate.
Tabi' here means something that is not the main substance, e.g., a thin silver rim on a wooden vessel.
2
Identify Principal vs. Subordinate in the Examples
In the examples from Al-Hidayah, the principal object is the vessel, saddle, or bed. The gold or silver plating on edges is the subordinate. The key is whether the prohibited substance is the principal material or just an attachment.
If the entire vessel were made of silver, the silver would be principal, not subordinate.
3
Apply the Maxim to the Gold/Silver Plating Case
Since the silver/gold is subordinate, it is not considered in the ruling. Therefore, the vessel is ruled as its base material (e.g., wood, metal, etc.), and using it is permissible provided one avoids contact with the prohibited part. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.
Avoidance is required: do not place mouth or hands on the silver/gold.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf considers such use disliked (makruh), and Imam Muhammad has two narrations, one agreeing with Abu Hanifa and one with Abu Yusuf. This ikhtilaf is based on how strictly the prohibition on gold/silver utensils is applied.
The Sahibayn likely argue that any contact with gold/silver is akin to using a prohibited utensil.
5
Recognize the Practical Outcome
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Hanifa's view, one may use such items with caution; under the Sahibayn's view, it is discouraged. The maxim provides a basis for leniency in everyday items with minor decorative metals.
This maxim is also applied to other contexts like gold writing on the Quran, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ راج
۲۲۰
(۲۸) لَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِالتَّوَابِع .
ترجمہ: احکام میں توابع کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز تابع ہوتی ہے حکماً اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصل کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے یعنی حکم اصل پر لگتا ہے تابع پر حکم نہیں لگتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ ان برتنوں میں کھانا پینا جائز ہے جن کے کنارے پر سونا لگا ہوا ہو، اسی طرح اس زمین پر سوار ہونا جائز ہے جس کی صرف کناروں پر سونا ہے، کیونکہ جس برتن اور زین کے صرف کناروں پر سونا لگا ہوا ہو تو اس میں سونا تابع ہے اصل نہیں ہے، اور تابع کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصل کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے، لہذا مذکورہ برتن میں بھی سونے کا اعتبار نہ ہو گا بلکہ اصل برتن کا اعتبار ہوگا اور اصل برتن تو سونے کا بنا ہوا نہیں ہے، لہذا اس میں کھانا پینا جائز ہے امام صاحب کے نزدیک اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے، البتہ کھاتے اور پیتے وقت اس جگہ سے بچے، یعنی برتن میں اُس جگہ منہ نہ لگائے اور زمین کو اُس جگہ سے نہ پکڑے، یہ جو کناروں پر معمولی سونا چاندی لگا ہے یا تابع ہے اور تابع کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الكراهية، ج ۴ ص ۴۵۴
قوله ويجوز الشرب في الإناء المفضض عند أبي حنيفة والركوب على السرج المفضض والجلوس على السرير المفضض هذا إذا كان يتقى موضع الفضة أى يتقى موضع الفم وقيل موضع الفم وموضع اليد أيضا في الأخذ وفي السرير والسرج موضع الجلوس . وقال أبو يوسف يكره ذلك وقول محمد يروى مع أبي حنيفة ويروى مع أبي يوسف وعلى هذا الخلاف الإناء المضبب بالذهب والفضة والكرسى المضبب بهما وكذا إذا فعل ذلك في السقف والمسجد وحلقة المرآة وجعله على المصحف واللجام وكذا الكتابة بالذهب
Usool e Hidayah page 220: (28) لا معتبر بالتوابع. Translation: In rulings, subordinates have no consideration. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that a thing which is subordinate has no consideration in rulings, rather the principal is considered, meaning the ruling applies to the principal, not to the subordinate. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is telling us that eating and drinking is permissible in vessels whose edges have gold attached, and similarly riding on a saddle that has gold only on its edges, because when gold is only on the edges of a vessel and saddle, the gold is subordinate, not principal. The subordinate is not considered; the principal is considered. Therefore, in the mentioned vessel, gold is not considered, rather the principal vessel is considered, and the principal vessel is not made of gold, so eating and drinking in it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to the Sahibayn it is not permissible. However, when eating and drinking, one should avoid that spot, i.e., not put the mouth on that part of the vessel and not hold the saddle at that spot. This minor gold or silver on the edges is subordinate, and the subordinate is not considered. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Karahiyah, vol. 4 p. 454: He said: Drinking from a silver-plated vessel is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and riding on a silver-plated saddle and sitting on a silver-plated bed, provided one avoids the silver, i.e., avoids the mouth's place, and it is said the mouth's place and also the hand's place when taking, and on the bed and saddle the sitting place. Abu Yusuf said: it is disliked. Muhammad's opinion is transmitted with Abu Hanifa and also with Abu Yusuf. On this basis is the difference regarding a vessel plated with gold and silver, a chair plated with them, and likewise if that is done on the ceiling, the mosque, the ring of a mirror, on the Quran, the bridle, and likewise writing with gold.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi legal maxim: 'La mu'tabara bil-tawabi'' (Subordinates are not considered in rulings). The commentary explains that when a prohibited substance like gold or silver is merely a subordinate (tabi') attached to a permissible principal object, the ruling follows the principal. For example, a vessel with gold only on its edges: the vessel itself is not made of gold, so the gold is subordinate. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, using such a vessel is permissible provided one avoids contact with the gold. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it disliked. The Hidayah quote elaborates: drinking from a silver-plated vessel, riding a silver-plated saddle, sitting on a silver-plated bed is permissible only if one avoids the silver. Abu Yusuf holds it disliked, while Muhammad has two narrations. The same difference applies to plating with gold and silver on various items like chairs, ceilings, mosque, mirror frames, Quran covers, bridles, and gold writing. This principle is used to determine the permissibility of using items that have some prohibited material in a minor, subordinate way.

Key Terms
تابع (tabi'): Something attached to a principal object that is not considered independently in rulings.
مُعْتَبَر (mu'tabar): Considered or taken into account legally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'La mu'tabara bil-tawabi'', what is the ruling on drinking from a vessel that has a thin silver rim?
A) It is absolutely prohibited regardless of the amount of silver.
B) It is permissible only if one avoids placing the mouth on the silver rim, according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
C) It is permissible unconditionally, even if one drinks from the silver part.
D) It is disliked according to all Hanafi imams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim that subordinates are not considered in rulings allows leniency in using items with minor prohibited attachments, provided one avoids the prohibited part.

The Ruling Attaches to the Complete Cause
Defines the ruling attachment principle and its application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle 'al-hukmu yudāfu ilā tamām al-ʿillah' and apply it to distinguish between permissible thin plating (tamwīh) and prohibited substantial gold/silver use.

Core Idea
A ruling only takes effect when its cause is fully realized – partial cause yields no ruling.

This lesson explores a core Hanafi maxim: the ruling is linked to the complete cause, not to its partial existence. The principle explains why thin gold plating on a vessel is permissible by consensus, while a solid gold vessel is not. It also clarifies the status of subordinate parts that do not trigger the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Recite the Arabic principle: اَلْحُكْمُ يُضَافُ إِلَى تَمَامِ الْعِلَّةِ. Understand that the ruling (ḥukm) is postponed until the cause (ʿillah) is fully present; an incomplete cause does not produce the ruling.
This is a general legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the cause in the examples
The cause for prohibiting gold/silver utensils is the substantial presence of these metals that conveys luxury. Thin plating (tamwīh) does not fulfill this cause because the metal is negligible.
The passage states 'plating (al-tamwīh) has no harm by consensus'.
3
Apply the maxim to the ruling
Since the cause is incomplete for thin plating, the ruling (prohibition) does not attach; the item is permissible. For thick or solid gold, the cause is complete, so prohibition applies.
The maxim distinguishes between a full cause and a subordinate coating.
4
Note the treatment of subordinate parts
Items like iron stirrups with small amounts of silver are considered subordinate (tābiʿ). According to Abu Hanifa, subordinate parts are not considered; the ruling follows the dominant substance.
This aligns with the maxim: the cause must be complete in the main item.
5
Generalise the principle
Understand that this maxim applies across fiqh: e.g., a partial sale does not transfer ownership, and a partial cause does not trigger a legal effect.
The maxim is a tool for deriving rulings in new cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاستبراء
(٣٠) اَلْحُكْمُ يُضَافُ إِلَى تَمَامِ الْعِلَّةِ.
والفضة على الثوب على هذا الخلاف والخلاف على ما تخلص أما التمويه لا بأس به إجماعا. الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الكراهية، ج ۲ ص ۲۸۲)
وَهِيَ حَدِيدَةٌ عَرِيضَةٌ، وَالْمِشْحَةُ : المِسَنُّ ، وَالتَّفْرُ: مَا يُجْعَلُ تَحْتَ ذَنَبِ الدَّابَّةِ، وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ تَابِعٌ وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِالتَّوَابِع). (العناية: كتاب الكراهية، ج ١٠ ص ١٠، ١١)
الهداية كتاب الكراهية، ج ۴ ص ۴۵۴

Section on Istibra': (30) The ruling is attached to the completion of the cause. And silver on clothing is subject to this difference, and the difference is that which is summarized. As for plating, there is no harm by consensus. (Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: Kitab al-Karahiyah, vol. 2 p. 282) And it is a wide iron, and al-mishah is the whetstone, and al-tafr is what is placed under the tail of the beast. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) held that it is subordinate, and the subordinate is not considered. (Al-Inaya: Kitab al-Karahiyah, vol. 10 pp. 10, 11) Al-Hidayah Kitab al-Karahiyah, vol. 4 p. 454 Al-Hidayah Kitab al-Karahiyah, vol. 4 p. 468
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage introduces the principle: 'Al-hukmu yudafu ila tamam al-illah' (The ruling is attached to the completion of the cause). This is a general maxim meaning that a legal ruling comes into effect only when its underlying cause ('illa) is fully realized. In the context of the subsequent Arabic text, it likely relates to the prohibition of using utensils with gold or silver: the prohibition is attached only when the gold or silver is substantial and not merely a subordinate. The text then mentions that silver on clothing is subject to the same difference of opinion, but plating (tamwih) that is very thin is permissible by consensus. The quotes from Al-Jawhara and Al-Inaya define some terms (iron bar, whetstone, crupper) and reiterate Abu Hanifa's view that such items are subordinate and thus not considered. This reinforces the principle of taba' from the previous section. The references point to the Hidayah for further reading.

Key Terms
عِلَّة (illa): The effective cause or reason for a legal ruling; the ruling is attached to its completion.
تَمَام (tamam): Completion or full realization of the cause.
تمويه (tamwih): Thin plating, coating, or gilding that does not constitute a substantial layer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'Al-hukmu yudāfu ilā tamām al-ʿillah', which of the following is permissible by consensus?
A) A solid gold ring.
B) A silver-coated spoon with a thick silver layer.
C) A cup with very thin gold plating (tamwīh).
D) A bronze vase with gold handles.

Key Takeaway
A ruling attaches only when its cause is fully realized; partial or subordinate causes do not trigger the ruling.

Preferring an Agreed-Upon General Rule Over a Disputed Specific Rule
States a principle and applies it to a fiqh case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that an agreed-upon general rule is preferred over a disputed specific rule and apply it to the case of a well's sanctuary (harim).

Core Idea
An agreed-upon general rule trumps a disputed specific rule.

In Al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani presents a key usul principle: when a general text (amm) is accepted by all scholars without dispute, it takes precedence over a specific text (khas) that is disputed in its acceptance or interpretation. This principle is then applied to resolve an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the size of the sanctuary (harim) of a well used for watering livestock. Understanding this principle helps us see how the Hanafi school prioritizes evidence when multiple proofs appear to conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the Arabic text of the principle: 'العام المتفق على قبوله والعمل به أولى عندهمن الخاص المختلف في قبوله والعمل به'. Understand that it is a methodological rule for preferring one type of evidence over another.
The principle is a tarjih (preference) rule, not a rule of validity.
2
Define key terms
Define 'amm' (general), 'khas' (specific), 'muttafaq alayh' (agreed upon), and 'mukhtalaf fih' (disputed). The principle applies only when the general is agreed upon and the specific is disputed.
If both are agreed upon, different principles of interpretation (like takhsis) come into play.
3
Examine the application
See how al-Marghinani applies the principle to the harim of a well. Imam Abu Hanifa holds 40 cubits based on a hadith that is general and agreed upon. The Sahibayn hold 60 cubits based on evidence that is disputed. The principle leads to preferring the 40-cubit ruling.
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah and is considered ahad but accepted.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that this is a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school itself. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree with their teacher Abu Hanifa on the measurement.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts Abu Hanifa's view as the mufta bihi based on this principle.
5
Apply the principle to a new case
Think of a scenario where a general Quranic verse (e.g., the prohibition of riba) is agreed upon, but a specific hadith allowing a certain transaction is disputed. According to this principle, the general prohibition would take precedence.
This principle helps maintain consistency in fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۲۶
كتاب إحياء الموات
(۳۳) الْعَامُ الْمُتَّفَقُ عَلَى قُبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ أَوْلَىٰ عِنْدَهُ مِنَ الْخَاصِ
الْمُخْتَلَفِ فِي قُبُوْلِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ.
ترجمہ: وہ عام جس کے قبول کرنے اور اس پر عمل کرنے پر اتفاق ہوا امام صاحب کے نزدیک راجح ہے اس خاص سے جس کی قبولیت میں اور اس پر عمل کرنے میں اختلاف ہو۔ تشریح مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وہ عام جو مقبول ہو اور اس پر عمل متفق علیہ ہو بہتر ہے اس خاص سے کہ جس کے قبول کرنے میں اور عمل کرنے میں اختلاف ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بئر ناضح ( وہ کنویں جس سے اونٹوں کو سیراب کیا جاتا ہو ) کا حریم چالیس گز ہوگا جبکہ صاحبین رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک ساٹھ گز ہوگا۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے: "مَنْ حَفَرَ بِرًا قَلَهُ أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا عَطَنًا لِمَاشِيَتِهِ"
سنن ابن ماجه کتاب الرهن باب حريم البئر، رقم: ۲۴۸۶
Book of Reviving Dead Lands. (33) The general rule that is agreed upon in acceptance and practice is preferable according to him over the specific rule that is disputed in acceptance and practice. Translation: The general rule whose acceptance and practice is agreed upon is more preponderant (rajih) in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa than the specific rule whose acceptance and practice is disputed. Explanation: This principle means that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a general rule that is accepted and practiced unanimously is better than a specific rule whose acceptance and practice is disputed. The author of Al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, indicates that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sanctuary (harim) of a well used for watering camels (bi'r nadih) is 40 cubits, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is 60 cubits. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is the saying of the Prophet (SAW): 'Whoever digs a well, for him is forty cubits as a resting place for his livestock.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, Kitab al-Rahn, Bab Harim al-Bi'r, hadith 2486)
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul principle from Al-Hidayah: a general ruling (amm) that is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) in acceptance and practice is preferred by Imam Abu Hanifa over a specific ruling (khas) that is disputed (mukhtalaf fih). The text then applies this principle to the case of the sanctuary (harim) of a well used for watering camels. Imam Abu Hanifa holds the sanctuary to be 40 cubits based on a hadith from Ibn Majah which is a general rule and is accepted by all. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it to be 60 cubits based on other evidence. However, since the hadith for 40 cubits is agreed upon (its acceptance is not disputed), while the evidence for 60 cubits is disputed, Imam Abu Hanifa gives preference to the 40-cubit ruling. The passage type is a definition of a principle with an applied example. It serves as a memorization anchor for the principle of preferring agreed-upon general evidence. The Hanafi position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: 40 cubits. The Sahibayn's position is noted but not preferred. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view. The hadith is the primary proof, and its authenticity is accepted.

Key Terms
عام (amm): A general rule or text that covers all instances without specification
خاص (khas): A specific rule or text that restricts the general to certain instances
متفق عليه (muttafaq alayh): Agreed upon in terms of acceptance and practice (among scholars)
مختلف فيه (mukhtalaf fih): Disputed in terms of acceptance or practice

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa prefer 40 cubits as the sanctuary of a well over 60 cubits?
A) Because the hadith for 40 cubits is a general rule that is agreed upon, while the evidence for 60 cubits is disputed
B) Because 60 cubits is too large for practical use
C) Because the Sahibayn are not reliable in this issue
D) Because the well is specifically for camels

Key Takeaway
The principle from Al-Hidayah: an agreed-upon general rule (amm muttafaq alayh) is preferred over a disputed specific rule (khas mukhtalaf fih), as applied to the well's sanctuary (harim).

The General Agreed Upon vs. The Specific Disputed: The Ḥarīm of a Well
Intra-Ḥanafī dispute on well ḥarīm illustrating uṣūl principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers the general hadith over the specific hadith in the dispute of the well's ḥarīm, and apply the underlying uṣūl principle to similar textual conflicts.

Core Idea
A general text agreed upon is preferred over a specific text whose acceptance is disputed.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the size of the ḥarīm (protected precinct) of a well in dead land. The disagreement between Imam Abū Ḥanīfa and the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī) about whether an irrigation well deserves a larger ḥarīm than a livestock well becomes a case study for a key uṣūl principle: when a general text is accepted and practiced by all, it takes precedence over a specific text that is disputed in its acceptance. Understanding this principle will sharpen your ability to resolve apparent conflicts between textual evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The ḥarīm of a well in dead land: Abū Ḥanīfa says 40 cubits on each side for all types; the Ṣāḥibayn say 40 for livestock wells, 60 for irrigation wells.
2
State Abū Ḥanīfa’s position and proof
He relies on the general hadith: 'Whoever digs a well, for him is what is around it: forty cubits.' The word 'man' (whoever) indicates generality.
This hadith is agreed upon in acceptance and practice.
3
State the Ṣāḥibayn’s position and proof
They rely on the specific hadith of al-Zuhrī that distinguishes: livestock well 40 cubits, irrigation well 60 cubits. They also argue by need (istiḥsān): irrigation requires more space for the camel.
This hadith is disputed in its acceptance (some scholars question its authenticity or interpretation).
4
Apply the uṣūl principle
A general text that is agreed upon in acceptance and practice is preferred over a specific text that is disputed in acceptance and practice. Therefore, Abū Ḥanīfa’s general proof prevails regardless of the type of well.
This principle resolves textual conflicts when the general is stronger in terms of acceptance.
5
Determine the muftā bihī (operative position)
The relied-upon position in the Ḥanafī school is 40 cubits for all wells, following Abū Ḥanīfa, as upheld in al-Hidāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب إحياء الموات
(۳۳) الْعَامُ الْمُتَّفَقُ عَلَى قُبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ أَوْلَىٰ عِنْدَهُ مِنَ الْخَاصِ الْمُخْتَلَفِ فِي قُبُوْلِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ.
ترجمہ: وہ عام جس کے قبول کرنے اور اس پر عمل کرنے پر اتفاق ہوا امام صاحب کے نزدیک راجح ہے اس خاص سے جس کی قبولیت میں اور اس پر عمل کرنے میں اختلاف ہو۔ تشریح مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وہ عام جو مقبول ہو اور اس پر عمل متفق علیہ ہو بہتر ہے اس خاص سے کہ جس کے قبول کرنے میں اور عمل کرنے میں اختلاف ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بئر ناضح ( وہ کنویں جس سے اونٹوں کو سیراب کیا جاتا ہو ) کا حریم چالیس گز ہوگا جبکہ صاحبین رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک ساٹھ گز ہوگا۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے: "مَنْ حَفَرَ بِرًا فَلَهُ مَا حَوْلَهَا أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا"
حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو شخص کنواں کھودے تو اس کے چوپاؤں کو سیراب کرنے کے لیے چالیس ذراع حریم ہو گا۔
امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے جس روایت سے استدلال کیا ہے وہ عام ہے، اور اس میں لفظ من عموم کے لیے ہے، اور اس کی قبولیت پر اور اس پر عمل کرنے پر اتفاق ہے، برخلاف صاحبین کی روایت کے کہ وہ خاص اور مختلف فیہ ہے اور وہ عام جس کی قبولیت اور اس پر عمل کرنے پر اتفاق ہو وہ رائج ہوتا ہے، لہذا چالیس ذراع والی روایت کو ترجیح حاصل ہو گی۔
وَقَوْلُهُ وَلَهُ مَا رَوَيْنَا) يُرِيدُ بِهِ قَوْلَهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مَنْ حَفَرَ بِثْرًا فَلَهُ مِمَّا حَوْلَهَا أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا مِنْ غَيْرِ فَصْلِ يَعْنِي بَيْنَ الْعَطَنِ وَالنَّاضِح ... وَقَوْلُهُ (وَالْعَامُ الْمُتَّفَقُ عَلَى قَبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ يُرِيدُ قَوْلَهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : مَنْ حَفَرَ بِتْرًا، لأَنَّ كَلِمَةَ مَنْ تُفِيدُ الْعُمُومَ (أَوْلَى عِنْدَهُ) أَيْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ مِنْ الْخَاصُ الْمُخْتَلَفِ فِى قَبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ يُرِيدُ بِهِ حَدِيثَ الزُّهْرِيِّ: حَرِيمُ الْعَيْنِ خَمُسُمِائَةِ ذِرَاعٍ، وَحَرِيمُ الْبِشِّرِ الْعَطَنُ أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا، وَحَرِيمُ بِشُرِ النَّاضِحِ سِتُّونَ ذِرَاعًا. (العناية كتاب إحياء الموات، ج ۱۲ ص ۷۴، ۷۵)
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: (وَمَنْ حَفَرَ بِتْرًا فِى مَوَاتٍ فَلَهُ حَرِيمُهَا أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا مِنْ كُلِّ جَانِبِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مَنْ حَفَرَ بِتْرًا فَلَهُ مَا حَوْلَهَا أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا) فَيُقَدَّرُ بِأَرْبَعِينَ كَى لَا تَتَعَطَّلَ عَلَيْهِ الْمَصَالِحُ ، وَلَا فَرُقَ فِي ذَلِكَ بَيْنَ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْبِرُ لِلْعَطَنِ أَوْ لِلنَّاضِحَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، وَعِنْدَهُمَا إِنْ كَانَتْ لِلْعَطَن فَأَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا وَإِنْ كَانَتْ لِلنَّاضِحِ فَحَرِيمُهَا سِتُّونَ ذِرَاعًا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ حَرِيمُ الْعَيْنِ خَمْسُمِائَةِ ذِرَاعٍ وَحَرِيمُ بِثْرِ الْعَطَنِ أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا وَحَرِيمُ بِمُرِ النَّاضِحِ سِتّونَ ذِرَاعًا وَلَانَّ اسْتِحْفَاقَ الْحَرِيمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْحَاجَةِ وَحَاجَةُ بِثْرِ النَّاضِحِ أَكْثَرُ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى مَوْضِعِ يَسِيرُ فِيهِ النَّاضِحُ، وَهُوَ الْبَعِيرُ، وَقَدْ يَطُولُ
Book of Reviving Dead Land. (33) The general (ʿāmm) that is agreed upon in acceptance and practice is preferable, according to him, to the specific (khāṣṣ) that is disputed in acceptance and practice. Translation: That general which is agreed upon in acceptance and practice is, according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), preponderant over that specific whose acceptance and practice is disputed. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to Imam, the general that is accepted and whose practice is agreed upon is better than the specific whose acceptance and practice is disputed. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to show that according to Imam, the ḥarīm (precinct) of a biʾr nāḍiḥ (a well used to water camels) is forty cubits, while according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is sixty cubits. Imam's proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever digs a well, he has what is around it: forty cubits.' The meaning of the hadith is that whoever digs a well, for watering his livestock, forty cubits of ḥarīm will be his. Imam says: The narration we have cited is general, and the word 'man' (whoever) indicates generality, and it is agreed upon in acceptance and practice, unlike the narration of the two companions, which is specific and disputed. And that general which is agreed upon in acceptance and practice is operative, therefore the forty-cubit narration is given preference. And his saying 'and we have what we narrated' intends the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever digs a well, for him from around it forty cubits without differentiation' meaning between the ʿaṭan (livestock watering place) and nāḍiḥ (irrigation well). And his saying 'and the general agreed upon in acceptance and practice' intends the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever digs a well' because the word 'man' indicates generality. (It is preferable according to him) i.e., according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) over the specific disputed in its acceptance and practice. He intends the hadith of al-Zuhri: 'The ḥarīm of a flowing spring is five hundred cubits, and the ḥarīm of a well for livestock (ʿaṭan) is forty cubits, and the ḥarīm of a well for irrigation (nāḍiḥ) is sixty cubits.' (Al-ʿInāyah, Kitāb Iḥyāʾ al-Mawāt, vol. 12, pp. 74-75) He (the author of al-Hidayah) said: 'Whoever digs a well in dead land, for him is its ḥarīm of forty cubits from each side, because of the Prophet's saying: Whoever digs a well, for him is what is around it: forty cubits.' So it is estimated at forty so that interests are not disrupted. And there is no difference in that between whether the well is for ʿaṭan or nāḍiḥ according to Abu Hanifa. But according to the two companions, if it is for ʿaṭan then forty cubits, and if for nāḍiḥ then its ḥarīm is sixty cubits, because of the Prophet's saying: 'The ḥarīm of a spring is five hundred cubits, the ḥarīm of a well for ʿaṭan is forty cubits, and the ḥarīm of a well for nāḍiḥ is sixty cubits.' And because the apportionment of ḥarīm is based on need, and the need of a nāḍiḥ well is greater, as it needs a space for the camel to move around, and it may be long.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ḥarīm (precinct) of a well in dead land, and uses it to illustrate a principle of uṣūl al-fiqh: a general (ʿāmm) text that is agreed upon in acceptance and practice is given preference over a specific (khāṣṣ) text whose acceptance is disputed. The passage begins by stating the principle: the general that is agreed upon is preferable to the specific that is disputed. The commentator explains that this principle is cited by the author of al-Hidayah to clarify the ruling on the ḥarīm of a well. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that regardless of whether the well is used for watering livestock (ʿaṭan) or for irrigation (nāḍiḥ), the ḥarīm is forty cubits on each side. His proof is the general hadith: 'Whoever digs a well, for him is what is around it: forty cubits.' The word 'man' (whoever) is general, covering all types of wells. This hadith is accepted and practiced by all scholars, so it is preferred. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) differentiate: if the well is for livestock, the ḥarīm is forty cubits; if for irrigation (using camels to draw water), it is sixty cubits. Their proof is the specific hadith from al-Zuhri that distinguishes between types of wells. They also argue by legal reasoning (istihsān): the need for space is greater for an irrigation well because it requires a turning area for the camel. However, the Hidayah upholds Abu Hanifa's view because his general hadith is agreed upon, while the specific hadith is disputed in its acceptance and interpretation. The principle applied here is that a general text with consensus on its acceptance and practice takes precedence over a specific text that is subject to disagreement regarding its acceptance and practice. This is a key rule in Hanafi uṣūl for resolving apparent conflicts between texts.

Key Terms
الْعَام (al-ʿāmm): A textual expression (lafẓ) that includes all individuals of its category without restriction, such as the word 'man' (whoever).
الْخَاص (al-khāṣṣ): A textual expression that specifies a particular subset, such as a hadith that explicitly distinguishes between types of wells.
الْحَرِيم (al-ḥarīm): The protected area around a well or spring that is considered part of its premises for purposes of ownership, use, and prevention of harm.
بِئْر نَاضِح (biʾr nāḍiḥ): A well used for irrigation where water is drawn by a beast of burden (e.g., a camel) that walks a path (sāniya).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Hidayah prefer Abu Hanifa's forty-cubit ruling over the Sahibayn's sixty-cubit ruling for irrigation wells?
A) Because the forty-cubit hadith is mutawātir, while the sixty-cubit hadith is āḥād.
B) Because the forty-cubit hadith is general and agreed upon, while the sixty-cubit hadith is specific and disputed.
C) Because the Sahibayn's hadith contradicts the Qurʾān.
D) Because Abu Hanifa's ruling is more practical.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi uṣūl, when a general text is accepted and practiced by all, it takes precedence over a specific text that is disputed in its acceptance, even if the specific text appears more detailed.

The Harim of a Well: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the extent of harim for wells

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the harim of wells, differentiate the Sahibayn's view, and apply the usul principle that a general hadith accepted by all takes precedence over a specific disputed hadith.

Core Idea
A general hadith agreed upon by all is preferred over a specific hadith whose acceptance is disputed.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the protected area (harim) of a well dug in dead land. While the matn states a general rule of forty cubits, the Sahibayn split hairs between wells for watering animals and those for irrigation. Abu Hanifa holds firm to a single standard, relying on a general hadith that has been unanimously accepted and practiced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its hadith evidence
The matn states: 'Whoever digs a well in dead land, for him is its harim forty cubits from every side.' This is supported by the general hadith: 'Whoever digs a well, for him is forty cubits around it.' Recognize that this is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Note the Sahibayn's differentiation and their specific hadith
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differentiate: for a well used for watering animals ('atan), harim is forty cubits; for an irrigation well (nadhih), harim is sixty cubits. They cite a specific hadith detailing these amounts plus five hundred cubits for a spring.
Their reasoning includes the greater need for space for the camel and long rope in irrigation wells.
3
Compare the two hadiths in terms of acceptance and practice
Abu Hanifa argues that the general hadith has been agreed upon for acceptance and practice by all scholars, while the specific hadith is disputed in its acceptance and practice. This is the core of the tarjih (preference).
The principle: a universally accepted general text outweighs a contested specific text.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's tarjih principle
The passage concludes: 'And from his principle is that the general (hadith) agreed upon its acceptance and acting upon it is given precedence over the specific (hadith) disputed in its acceptance and acting upon it.' Recognize this as a usul al-iftā' rule that applies here.
This is a methodological preference, not a rejection of the specific hadith's authenticity.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Apply the views: If a person digs an irrigation well in dead land, according to Abu Hanifa he is entitled to 40 cubits of harim; according to the Sahibayn, 60 cubits. This affects how much land he can fence off and protect from others.
The dispute has real consequences in land use and property rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: (وَمَنْ حَفَرَ بِتْرًا فِى مَوَاتٍ فَلَهُ حَرِيمُهَا أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا مِنْ كُلِّ جَانِبِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مَنْ حَفَرَ بِتْرًا فَلَهُ مَا حَوْلَهَا أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا) فَيُقَدَّرُ بِأَرْبَعِينَ كَى لَا تَتَعَطَّلَ عَلَيْهِ الْمَصَالِحُ ، وَلَا فَرُقَ فِي ذَلِكَ بَيْنَ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْبِرُ لِلْعَطَنِ أَوْ لِلنَّاضِحَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، وَعِنْدَهُمَا إِنْ كَانَتْ لِلْعَطَن فَأَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا وَإِنْ كَانَتْ لِلنَّاضِحِ فَحَرِيمُهَا سِتُّونَ ذِرَاعًا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ حَرِيمُ الْعَيْنِ خَمْسُمِائَةِ ذِرَاعٍ وَحَرِيمُ بِثْرِ الْعَطَنِ أَرْبَعُونَ ذِرَاعًا وَحَرِيمُ بِمُرِ النَّاضِحِ سِتّونَ ذِرَاعًا وَلَانَّ اسْتِحْفَاقَ الْحَرِيمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْحَاجَةِ وَحَاجَةُ بِثْرِ النَّاضِحِ أَكْثَرُ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى مَوْضِعِ يَسِيرُ فِيهِ النَّاضِحُ، وَهُوَ الْبَعِيرُ، وَقَدْ يَطُولُ الرِّشَاءُ، وَفِي بِثْرِ الْعَطَنِ يَسْتَقِي بِيَدِهِ فَلا بُدَّ مِنْ التَّفَاوُتِ بَيْنَهُمَا، وَلَهُ مَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ غَيْرِ فَضْلٍ، وَمِنْ أَصْلِهِ أَنَّ الْعَامَّ الْمُتَّفَقَ عَلَى قَبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ يُرَجَّحُ عَلَى الْخَاصٌ الْمُخْتَلَفِ فِي قَبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ
He (the author) said: (Whoever digs a well in dead land, then for him is its protected area forty cubits from every side, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever digs a well, for him is what is around it forty cubits'.) It is estimated at forty so that benefits are not disrupted [for him]. And there is no difference in that between whether the well is for the 'atan (watering place for animals) or for the nadhih (irrigation well) according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if it is for the 'atan, then forty cubits; and if it is for the nadhih, then its protected area is sixty cubits, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The protected area of a spring is five hundred cubits, the protected area of a well for 'atan is forty cubits, and the protected area of a well for nadhih is sixty cubits.' And because entitlement to the protected area is based on need, and the need of the nadhih well is greater because it requires a place for the nadhih (the camel used for irrigation) to walk, and it is a camel, and the rope may be long, while for the 'atan well, one draws water by hand, so there must be a difference between them. And for him is what we have narrated without distinction, and from his principle is that the general (hadith) agreed upon its acceptance and acting upon it is given precedence over the specific (hadith) disputed in its acceptance and acting upon it.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the harim (protected area) of a well in dead land. The matn from al-Hidayah states the ruling: whoever digs a well in mawat (dead land) is entitled to a harim of forty cubits on each side, based on the hadith 'Whoever digs a well, for him is forty cubits around it.' Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this ruling applies equally whether the well is for watering animals ('atan) or for irrigation (nadhih). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differentiate: for a 'atan well, forty cubits suffices; for a nadhih well, sixty cubits are needed because it requires space for the animal to walk and for the long rope. Their evidence is a different hadith specifying these amounts. Abu Hanifa's response is that the general hadith—which has been agreed upon for acceptance and practice—is preferred over the specific hadith whose acceptance is disputed. The principle established here is that a generally accepted and practiced hadith takes precedence over a specific hadith that is subject to disagreement regarding its acceptance and practice.

Key Terms
حَرِيم (harim): The protected area around a well or water source that cannot be claimed by others; it is reserved for the owner's use.
عَطَن (atan): A watering place for animals, specifically where camels or livestock drink.
نَاضِح (nadhih): A well used for irrigation, where water is drawn by a camel or machine.
بِثْر (bithr): A well, synonymous with bir in Arabic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that the harim for both 'atan and nadhih wells is forty cubits?
A) A specific hadith from al-Zuhri
B) The general hadith 'Whoever digs a well, for him is forty cubits around it'
C) Analogy to springs
D) The need for more space for irrigation

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view that all wells have a 40-cubit harim is the mufta bihi because the general hadith agreed upon by all is preferred over a specific disputed hadith.

Water Dominance and Reviving Abandoned Riverbeds
States a legal principle and its application to riverbeds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reviving abandoned riverbeds and apply the principle 'qahr al-mā' yadfa‘u qahr ghayrihi' to determine when such land can be owned.

Core Idea
Water's natural dominance over a riverbed prevents any person from claiming ownership as long as the water can possibly return.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi legal principle governing the relationship between natural water bodies and land ownership. The text from al-Hidayah discusses what happens when a major river like the Euphrates or Tigris changes course, leaving its former bed dry. The ruling depends on whether the water can possibly return, reflecting the principle that water's dominance (qahr) overrides the dominance of any individual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is reviving (ihya) land that was once a riverbed. The ruling depends on the possibility of water returning.
2
Locate the legal principle
The principle is 'qahr al-mā' yadfa‘u qahr ghayrihi' — water's dominance repels the dominance of another. Understand that land under water's control cannot be owned privately.
3
Understand the condition
The key condition is whether the water can possibly return to the abandoned bed (yajuzu awduhu ilayh). If yes, the land remains part of the river; if not, it may become mawat.
4
Identify the rationale
The rationale is public need (hajat al-'ammah): the land must remain available as a river for public use, even if currently dry.
5
Apply the condition
Apply the condition to determine the ruling: if water can return → revival not allowed; if water cannot return and land is not a harim → treated as mawat and can be revived.
Harim means the protected perimeter of an inhabited area.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَهْرُ الْمَاءِ يَدْفَعُ قَهْرَ غَيْرِهِ. الهداية: كتاب إحياء الموات، ج ۴ ص ۴۸۷ قال: وما ترك الفرات أو الدجلة) أى قال القدورى رَحِمَهُ الله ..... وعدل عنه الماء) أى ما ترك الفرات أو دجلة، ومعنى عدل عنه: انكشف عنه وأخذ موضعا غيره. ويجوز عوده إليه أى والحال أنه يجوز عوده إليه، أى إلى ما ترک عنه، ومعنى يجوز : يمكن، لم يجز إحياؤه لحاجة العامة إلى كونه نهراء وإن كان لا يجوز أى لا يمكن أن يعود إليه فهو كالموات إذا لم يكن حريما
The dominance of water repels the dominance of another. [From] al-Hidayah, Book of Reviving Dead Land, volume 4, page 487: He said: 'And what the Euphrates or the Tigris leaves' — i.e., al-Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said: '... and the water turned away from it' — i.e., what the Euphrates or Tigris left, and the meaning of 'turned away from it' is: it uncovered and took another place. And it is possible for it to return to it — i.e., while it is possible for it to return to it, meaning to what it left, and the meaning of 'possible' is 'could happen' — it is not permissible to revive it due to the public need for it to be a river. And if it is not possible, i.e., it cannot return to it, then it is like dead land if it is not a harim.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This lesson presents the legal principle 'qahr al-mā' yadfa‘u qahr ghayrihi' (the dominance of water repels the dominance of another) and applies it to the case of abandoned riverbeds. The principle means that land under the control and dominance of water cannot be owned by anyone else, as water's dominance overrides claims of ownership. The text from al-Hidayah discusses the situation when a large river like the Euphrates or Tigris changes course, leaving behind its former bed. If the water could possibly return to that bed, then it is not permissible to revive (ihya) that land, because it is still considered part of the river for the public benefit. Only when it is definitively impossible for the water to return (e.g., due to permanent geological change), and the land is not the harim of any inhabited area, can it be treated as dead land (mawat) and revived with the permission of the ruler.

Key Terms
قَهْر (qahr): Dominance or control; here it refers to the natural dominance of water over the land it covers.
إِحْيَاء الْمَوَات (ihya al-mawat): Reviving dead land by making it productive, e.g., by cultivation or building.
حَرِيم (harīm): The protected perimeter around an inhabited area or well; land that is reserved for the benefit of the settlement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible to revive land that was formerly part of a river like the Euphrates or Tigris?
A) Immediately after the water leaves
B) Only if the water can possibly return
C) Only if it is impossible for the water to return and it is not a harim
D) Always, with permission of the ruler

Key Takeaway
A riverbed vacated by water retains its public status as long as the water can possibly return; only when return is impossible does it become dead land eligible for revival.

The Dominance of Water Prevents Other Ownership
States a legal maxim and its application to reviving dead land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim qahru al-ma' to determine the permissibility of reviving land that was formerly covered by water.

Core Idea
Land that can be inundated again is not mawat and cannot be privately owned.

This passage from al-Hidayah anchors a key Hanafi principle about public waterways. The author explains that when a river recedes, the exposed land remains in the river's 'dominance' if water may return; only when return is impossible and it's not a harim does it become mawat eligible for revival.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
State the maxim 'qahr al-ma' yadfa'u qahr ghayrihi' and its general meaning that water's dominance overrides any claim of ownership.
This is the foundational legal principle.
2
Distinguish between possible and impossible water return
If water can return to the land, it remains in the ruling of a river and cannot be revived. If return is impossible, it becomes like mawat.
The key is the possibility of return, not actual return.
3
Apply the harim condition
If the land is a harim (precinct) of an inhabited area, it is attached to that area and cannot be revived independently.
Harim is already owned or reserved.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on permission
Abu Hanifa requires the Imam's permission for reviving mawat; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not, and the later fatwa leans toward the latter view.
This ikhtilaf only applies if the land is indeed mawat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۴) قَهْرُ الْمَاءِ يَدْفَعُ قَهْرَ غَيْرِهِ.
ترجمہ: پانی کا غلبہ غیر کے غلبہ کو روکتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکور و اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس جگہ پر پانی کا غلبہ ہو تو اس جگہ پر کوئی اور غلبہ حاصل نہیں کر سکتا، یعنی کوئی اس کا مالک نہیں بن سکتا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا ر ہے ہیں کہ نہر دجلہ یا فرات یا کوئی دوسرا دریا اگر اپنے آس پاس کی جگہیں چھوڑ دیں یعنی پانی کم ہو جائے، اب اگر ان جگہوں کی طرف پانی کا دوبارہ آنا ممکن ہو تو ان کو آباد کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جب تک پانی دوبارہ آنے کا امکان ہے تو وہ موات نہیں بلکہ وہ بھی نہر کے حکم میں ہے، جس کا احیاء جائز نہیں لوگوں کی حاجت وضرورت کی وجہ سے ، اور اگر پانی دوبارہ لوٹنے کا امکان نہ ہو اور وہ جگہ کسی آبادی کا حریم بھی نہ ہو تو اس کا احیاء درست ہے، کیونکہ اب وہ موات ہے جس کا کوئی مالک نہیں، اس لیے کہ پانی کا غلبہ سب کے غلبہ کو دور کر دیتا ہے اور اس وقت وہ حاکم وقت کے قبضہ میں ہے، لہذا اس کا احیاء جائز ہو گا مگر حاکم وقت کی اجازت کے ساتھ۔
الرِّشَاءُ، وَفِي بِثْرِ الْعَطَنِ يَسْتَقِي بِيَدِهِ فَلا بُدَّ مِنْ التَّفَاوُتِ بَيْنَهُمَا، وَلَهُ مَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ غَيْرِ فَضْلٍ، وَمِنْ أَصْلِهِ أَنَّ الْعَامَّ الْمُتَّفَقَ عَلَى قَبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ يُرَجَّحُ عَلَى الْخَاصٌ الْمُخْتَلَفِ فِي قَبُولِهِ وَالْعَمَلِ بِهِ تبيين الحقائق كتاب إحياء الموات، ج 4 ص ٣٦) الهداية: كتاب إحياء الموات، ج ۴ ص ۴۸۷ قال: وما ترك الفرات أو الدجلة) أى قال القدورى رَحِمَهُ الله ..... وعدل عنه الماء) أى ما ترك الفرات أو دجلة، ومعنى عدل عنه: انكشف عنه وأخذ موضعا غيره. ويجوز عوده إليه أى والحال أنه يجوز عوده إليه، أى إلى ما ترک عنه، ومعنى يجوز : يمكن، لم يجز إحياؤه لحاجة العامة إلى كونه نهراء وإن كان لا يجوز أى لا يمكن أن يعود إليه فهو كالموات إذا لم يكن حريما
البناية: كتاب إحياء الموات، ج ۱۲ ص ۳۰۵، ۳۰۶) وما ترك الفرات أو الدجلة وعدل) ماؤه عنه) أى عن المتروك (و) لكن (يجوز عوده) أى الماء (إليه) أى إلى ذلك المكان الذي تركه لم يجز إحياؤه) ولو بإذن الإمام لحاجة العامة إلى مونه نهراً (وإن كان لا يجوز) أى غير محتمل أن يعود إليه فهو كالموات أى لأنه ليس في ملك أحد، وهذا إذا لم يكن حريماً) فإن كان حريماً لعامر كان تبعاً له، لأنه من مرافقه، وإذا لم يكن حريماً لعامر فإنه يملكه من أحياه) إن كان (بإذن الإمام عند الإمام) وإلا فلا، خلافا لهما كما تقدم اللباب في شرح الكتاب : ج ۲ ص ۲۲۲
(34) The dominance of water prevents the dominance of others. Translation: The dominance of water prevents the dominance of others. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that wherever water dominates, no one else can dominate there, i.e., no one can own it. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if the Tigris, Euphrates, or any other river leaves its surrounding areas (i.e., the water recedes), then if it is possible for the water to return to those places, it is not permissible to revive them, because as long as there is possibility of water returning, they are not dead land (mawat) but rather they are in the ruling of the river, which cannot be revived due to the general need. And if it is not possible for the water to return and that place is not a harim (precinct) of an inhabited area, then its revival is valid, because now it is mawat that has no owner, because the dominance of water removes all other dominance, and at that time it is under the control of the ruler, so its revival is permissible but with the ruler's permission. … Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Book of Ihya al-Mawat, vol. 4, p. 36; Al-Hidayah: Book of Ihya al-Mawat, vol. 4, p. 487. He said: 'What the Euphrates or Tigris leaves' i.e., al-Quduri said … 'and the water turns away from it' i.e., it leaves and takes another place. 'And it is possible for it to return to it' i.e., and it is possible for it to return to what it left; 'the meaning of 'possible' is feasible; 'it is not permissible to revive it' due to the general need for it to be a river; 'and if it is not possible' i.e., it cannot return to it, then it is like mawat if it is not a harim. Al-Binayah: Book of Ihya al-Mawat, vol. 12, pp. 305-306. And what the Euphrates or Tigris leaves and its water turns away from it, i.e., from the left area, but it is possible for the water to return to it, i.e., to that place which it left, it is not permissible to revive it even with the Imam's permission due to the general need for it to be a river. And if it is not possible, i.e., it is improbable that it will return, then it is like mawat, because it is not in anyone's ownership. This is if it is not a harim. If it is a harim of an inhabited area, it is a dependent of it. And if it is not a harim, then whoever revives it owns it if with the Imam's permission according to Imam Abu Hanifa, otherwise not, contrary to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as mentioned earlier in al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, vol. 2, p. 222.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage introduces a Hanafi legal maxim: 'The dominance of water prevents the dominance of others.' It then applies this to the case of land from which river water has receded. The passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi tradition, citing al-Hidayah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and al-Binayah. The core ruling: if water can return, the land remains under public use (like a river bed) and cannot be revived (ihya) even with the ruler's permission, because it is not truly mawat (dead land). If water cannot return and the land is not a harim (precinct) of an inhabited area, then it is mawat and can be revived, but only with the ruler's permission per Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the ruler's permission is not necessary for owning revived mawat land. The passage also includes a reference to a principle about general and specific texts, but that is incidental. The primary lesson is the clear distinction based on the possibility of water return and the public interest.

Key Terms
قهر الماء (qahr al-mā’): The overwhelming dominance of water over land, preventing private ownership.
إحياء الموات (iḥyā’ al-mawāt): Reviving dead land by making it productive, which grants ownership under certain conditions.
حریم (ḥarīm): The precinct or appurtenant area of an inhabited place, considered part of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'qahr al-ma' yadfa'u qahr ghayrihi', when is it NOT permissible to revive land from which river water has receded?
A) When the water may possibly return to that land
B) When the land is a harim of an inhabited area
C) When the land is within the domain of the ruler
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The dominance of water continues as long as return is possible; only when that possibility is extinguished and the land is not a harim does it become mawat eligible for revival.

The Principle of Lifting an Action by a Superior or Equal Action
Introduces a Hanafi legal maxim with a naskh comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-fi‘lu yurfa‘u bimā huwa fawqahū aw mithlihī' and explain its parallel to naskh.

Core Idea
An action's effect is nullified only by an action of equal or greater legal authority.

This lesson introduces a core Hanafi principle that governs how one legal action can override another. It is analogous to naskh (abrogation) in Quranic verses. Although the original source begins to apply this to hunting, the text is incomplete; nevertheless, the maxim itself is a powerful tool for resolving conflicts of evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Write down the Arabic phrase 'al-fi‘lu yurfa‘u bimā huwa fawqahū aw mithlihī' and its translation. Understand that 'yurfa‘u' means 'is lifted' in the sense of 'nullified' or 'removed'.
The maxim is often applied in conflicts of evidence (ta‘āruḍ al-adillah) and in actions like hunting.
2
Identify the condition for nullification
The second action must be either superior (fawq) or equal (mithl) to the first action. Inferior actions cannot lift a superior or equal action.
This mirrors the rules of naskh: an abrogating text (nāsikh) must be at least as strong as the abrogated (mansūkh) in transmission and meaning.
3
Connect to naskh
The author explicitly compares this principle to naskh. In Hanafi usul, a later text can only abrogate an earlier one if it is of similar or higher authority in thubūt and dalāla.
Understanding naskh helps internalise the maxim.
4
Anticipate the application
The original text begins to apply this to hunting: If a Muslim sends his trained dog, the dog's action (killing the game) is considered a valid slaughter because the dog's action is 'similar' to the hunter's intent. The principle ensures the action is lifted by an equal or superior action.
Due to OCR corruption, the full application is not preserved; refer to al-Hidayah's chapter on hunting for completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۵) الْفِعْلُ يَرْفَعُ بِمَا هُوَ فَوْقَهُ أَوْ مِثْلَهُ.
ترجمہ: فعل رفع ہوتا ہے اپنے سے مافوق یا اپنے مثل کے ساتھ ۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک فعل دوسرے فعل سے اس وقت ختم ہوتا ہے جب دوسر افعل پہلے فعل سے بڑھ کر ہو یا کم از کم اس کے مثل ہو، جیسے ناسخ کے لئے منسوخ سے اعلی یا اس کا مساوی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر مسلمان نے شکار پر اپنا کتا
الهداية: كتاب الصيد فصل في الجوارح، ج ۴ ص ۵۱۰
(35) The action is lifted by what is above it or like it. Translation: The action is lifted by what is above it or like it. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that an action ends another action when the second action is greater than the first or at least equal to it, like the necessity for the abrogator to be superior or equal to the abrogated. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if a Muslim sends his dog to hunt... Al-Hidayah: Book of Hunting, Chapter on Predators, vol. 4, p. 510.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi legal maxim: 'An action is lifted by what is above it or like it.' It explains that to nullify a previous action, the subsequent action must be of a higher or equal rank, drawing an analogy with naskh (abrogation). The text then begins to apply this to hunting: if a Muslim sends his (trained) dog to hunt, but the OCR breaks off. The reference points to al-Hidayah's chapter on hunting. The principle itself is used in various fiqh contexts; in hunting, it may relate to the slaughtering action of the dog being superior or similar to the hunter's intention. However, due to OCR corruption, the specific application is missing. The lesson is incomplete but introduces the principle.

Key Terms
الفعل يرفع بما هو فوقه أو مثله (al-fi‘lu yurfa‘u bimā huwa fawqahū aw mithlihī): A legal maxim meaning that the effect of an action is nullified only by an action of equal or greater authority.
ناسخ (nāsikh): The abrogating text or action that supersedes a previous one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The second action must be preferable in the sight of Allah
B) The second action must be of a higher or equal level
C) The second action must be similar in form

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-fi‘lu yurfa‘u bimā huwa fawqahū aw mithlihī' mandates that a later action can only overrule an earlier one if it is of equal or greater legal force.

Preferring Prohibition When Causes of Halal and Haram Combine
Ruling with proof: principle and application to hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle for conflicting causes of halal and haram, apply it to the hunting scenario of a shot animal falling into water or from a height, and distinguish between avoidable and unavoidable causes of prohibition.

Core Idea
When halal and haram causes combine, avoidable prohibition prevails; unavoidable prohibition is disregarded.

In Islamic law, multiple causes may converge on a single action. When a cause making an act permissible and a cause making it prohibited coincide, the jurist must weigh them. The Hanafi school provides a clear principle: if the cause of prohibition can be avoided, it takes precedence out of caution (ihtiyatan); if it cannot be avoided, it is like non-existence. This lesson examines this rule through the classic case of a hunted animal that falls after being shot, drawing from foundational Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causes
The passage presents two causes: the hunter's shot (cause of permissibility) and the fall into water or from a height (cause of prohibition). Each cause points to a different ruling – halal for the shot, haram for the fall.
The Quranic prohibition of al-mutaraddiyah (the fallen animal) is the textual basis for the prohibition cause.
2
Determine avoidability
Check whether the cause of prohibition (the fall) can be avoided. If the hunter could have taken measures to prevent the fall (e.g., hunting on level ground), it is avoidable. If the fall is an inevitable consequence of the shot (e.g., falling directly to the ground), it is unavoidable.
Falling into water or from a cliff is potentially avoidable; falling to the ground after a shot is not.
3
Apply the principle
If avoidable: give precedence to prohibition – the game is haram. If unavoidable: disregard the prohibition cause – the game is halal, as the arrow wound is deemed the actual cause of death.
The principle is derived from the capacity-based obligation: Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.
4
Account for doubt
If uncertainty exists about whether death was from the wound or the fall, the game is haram out of caution (ihtiyatan). This aligns with the Hanafi preference for avoiding what is doubtful.
This is explicitly stated in the text: 'if doubt arises... it is haram out of caution.'
5
Note the textual and rational proofs
The primary proof is Quran 5:3 prohibiting al-mutaraddiyah. The rational proof is that when causes conflict, the side of prohibition is preferred as precaution, and obligation is only within capacity.
The principle is a method of tarjih (preponderance) when dalils conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: جب حلت و حرمت دونوں کے سبب جمع ہو جائیں اور سبب حرمت سے بچنا ممکن ہو تو احتیاطا جانب حرمت کو تر جیح دی جائے گی لیکن اگر ایسا سبب ہو جس سے بچنا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس کا وجود عدم کے درجہ میں ہوگا۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ میں حلت اور حرمت دونوں کے اسباب موجود ہوں اور سبب حرمت سے خود کو بچا ناممکن بھی ہو تو احتیاطا حرمت کی جانب کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اور اگر حرمت کے سبب سے بچنا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس سبب حرمت کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ انکار ہے ہیں کہ اگر شکاری نے شکار پر تیر چلایا اور تیر لگنے کے بعد شکار پانی میں گر گیا یا کسی چھت اور پہاڑ پر جا گرا، پھر وہاں سے لڑھکتا ہوا زمین پر گرا تو مرا ہوا تھا تو اس کا کھانا جائز نہ ہوگا، اس کے برعکس اگر شکاری نے شکار کو مارا اور وہ زمین پر گرا اور مر گیا تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے، کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں حلت اور حرمت دونوں کے اسباب جمع ہیں کہ تیر سے مرنا حلت کا سبب اور پانی میں گر کر مرنا یا پہاڑ سے لڑھک کر مرنا حرمت کا سبب ہے اور یہ ایسا سبب ہے جس سے بچنا ممکن ہے، اس لیے یہاں حرمت کے سبب کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے حرام کا حکم لاگو کیا گیا، جب کہ دوسری صورت میں براہ راست زمین پر گر کر مرنا اگر چہ حرمت کا سبب ہے، مگر اس سے بچنا متعذر ہے، اس لیے یہ سبب معتبر شمار نہ کیا گیا اور اس کی حالت کا حکم دیا گیا۔
قال (وإذا رمى صيدا فوقع فى الماء إلخ) كلامه واضح، وهو في المعنى مقيد بأن لا يكون الجرح مهلكا في الحال على ما سيأتي. قوله (وكذا السقوط من عال) وهو في بعض النسخ من علو ، وهو لغة في الأول مضموما ومفتوحا ومكسورا. وقوله (وإن وقع على الأرض ابتداء أكل) يعنى إذا لم يكن على الأرض ما يقتله كحد الرمح والقصبة المنصوبة على ما . (العناية كتاب الصيد، فصل في الرمي، ج ۱۰ ص ۱۲۹)

(۳۷) الْمَوْتُ إِذَا كَانَ مُضَافًا إِلَى الْجَرْحِ بِيَقِيْنِ كَانَ الصَّيْدُ حَلَالًا وَإِذَا كَانَ مُضَافًا إِلَى التَّقْلِ بِيَقِيْنِ كَانَ حَرَامًا وَإِنْ وَقَعَ الشَّكُ مَاتَ بِالْجَرْحِ أَوِ التَّقْلِ كَانَ حَرَامًا اِحْتِيَاطًا.
ترجمہ: جب یقینی طور پر موت زخم کی طرف منسوب ہوگی تو شکار حلال ہوگا اور جب یقینی طور پر قتل کی طرف منسوب ہوتو شکار حرام ہوگا، اور اگر موت کے بارے میں شک ہو جائے اور یہ معلوم نہ ہو سکے کہ شکار زخم سے مرا ہے یا بوجھ سے تو بھی احتیاطاً شکار حرام ہوگا۔
قال: وإذا رمى صيدا فوقع فى الماء أو وقع على سطح أو جبل ثم تردى منه إلى الأرض لم يؤكل...... لأنه المتردية وهى حرام بالنص) وهو قوله سبحانه وتعالى: (وَالْمَوْقُوذَةُ وَالْمُتَرَدِّيَةُ وَالنَّطِيحَةُ ..... (المائدة: ٣) (ولأنه احتمل الموت بـغـيـر الـرمـى، إذ الماء مهلك لأنه اجتمع فيه سبب الحرمة والإباحة، فيغلب جانب الحرمة احتياطا وكذا السقوط من عال أى وكذا لا يؤكل إذا سقط من مكان ..... وإن وقع على الأرض ابتداء أكل) يعنى رمى صيدا على رأس الجبل، أو على شجر أو فى الهواء فوقع على الأرض ومات: حل... لأنه لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه أى عن سقوطه ووقوعه على الأرض (وفي اعتباره سد باب الاصطياد، بخلاف ما تقدم وهو ما إذا وقع على جبل ونحوه ثم تردى إلى الأرض لأنه يمكن التحرز عنه أى عن وقوعه على سطح أو جبل أو نحوهما فصار (الأصل في هذا الباب أن سبب الحرمة والحل إذا اجتمعا وأمكن التحرز عما هو سبب الحرمة ترجح جهة الحرمة احتياطا، وإن كان ما لا يمكن التحرز عنه جرى وجوده أى وجود سبب الحرمة مجرى عدمه؛ لأن التكليف بحسب الوسع والطاقة وتكليف ما لا يسعه لا يحسن من حكيم. (البناية كتاب الصيد، فصل في الرمي، ج ۱۲ ص ۴۴۵، ۴۴۶ الهداية كتاب الصيد، فصل في الرمي، ج۴ ص ۵۱۴
Translation: When the causes of permissibility and prohibition are both present, and it is possible to avoid the cause of prohibition, then out of caution the aspect of prohibition is given precedence. But if there is a cause that cannot be avoided, then its existence is like non-existence. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that if in a matter both the causes of permissibility and prohibition are present, and it is also possible to avoid the cause of prohibition, then out of caution the side of prohibition is given precedence. And if avoidance of the cause of prohibition is not possible, then that cause of prohibition is not considered. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that if a hunter shoots an arrow at game, and after being hit the game falls into water, or onto a roof or mountain, then rolls down to the ground and dies, then eating it is not permissible. Conversely, if the hunter kills the game and it falls directly to the ground and dies, then eating it is permissible. Because in the first case, the causes of permissibility and prohibition are combined: death by arrow is a cause of permissibility, and death by falling into water or rolling down a mountain is a cause of prohibition. And this is a cause that can be avoided, so here the cause of prohibition is given precedence and the ruling of prohibition is applied. Whereas in the second case, dying directly by falling to the ground, even if it is a cause of prohibition, is unavoidable, so this cause is not considered and the ruling is based on the first cause.
He said: (If he shoots at game and it falls into water, etc.) His words are clear, and in meaning they are restricted by that the wound not be immediately fatal, as will come. His statement: (And likewise falling from a height) and in some copies 'from an elevation', and it is linguistically the same word with dammah, fatah, and kasrah. And his statement: (And if it falls on the ground initially, it is eaten) meaning if there is nothing on the ground that kills it, like the point of a spear or an erect reed. (Al-‘Inayah, Kitab al-Sayd, Fasl fi al-Ramy, vol. 10 p. 129)

(37) Death, when it is certainly attributed to the wound, then the game is permissible; and when it is certainly attributed to the fall, then it is forbidden; and if doubt arises whether it died from the wound or the fall, then it is forbidden out of caution.
Translation: When death is certainly attributed to the wound, the game is halal; when it is certainly attributed to the fall, the game is haram; and if doubt arises about the death and it is not known whether the game died from the wound or from the fall, then out of caution the game is haram.
He said: If he shoots at game and it falls into water, or onto a roof or mountain, then rolls from there to the ground, it is not eaten... because it is [like] the mutaraddiyah (the animal that falls from a height), and it is forbidden by the text – and that is His statement, exalted: (And that which is killed by a blow, and that which falls from a height, and that which is gored) (Al-Ma'idah: 3) – and because it is possible that death occurred from other than the shot, since water kills. Because the cause of prohibition and permissibility are combined, so the side of prohibition prevails out of caution. And likewise falling from a height – i.e., likewise it is not eaten if it falls from a place... And if it falls on the ground initially, it is eaten – meaning he shot game on top of a mountain, or on a tree, or in the air, and it fell on the ground and died: it is permissible... because it is impossible to avoid its fall and landing on the ground. And regarding its consideration would be closing the door of hunting, unlike what preceded, which is when it falls on a mountain and the like and then rolls to the ground because it is possible to avoid its landing on a roof or mountain or the like. So the principle in this chapter is: when the cause of prohibition and permissibility are combined, and it is possible to avoid what is the cause of prohibition, then the aspect of prohibition prevails out of caution; but if it is something that cannot be avoided, then its existence – i.e., the existence of the cause of prohibition – is like non-existence, because obligation is according to capacity and ability, and obligating what is beyond capacity is not befitting of a Wise (Allah). (Al-Binayah, Kitab al-Sayd, Fasl fi al-Ramy, vol. 12 pp. 445-446; Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Sayd, Fasl fi al-Ramy, vol. 4 p. 514)
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage from Usool E Hidayah presents a ruling with proof concerning the permissibility of eating game that has been shot but then falls into water or from a height before dying. The author begins by stating a key legal principle: when the causes of permissibility (halal) and prohibition (haram) are both present, and it is possible to avoid the cause of prohibition, caution dictates that prohibition is given precedence. However, if avoiding the cause of prohibition is impossible, then that cause is disregarded. This principle is then applied to hunting. The example given: if a hunter shoots an arrow at an animal, and after being hit the animal falls into water or onto a roof/mountain and then tumbles to the ground and dies, the meat is not permissible. Why? Because two causes are present: the arrow wound (cause of permissibility) and the fall (cause of prohibition). Since the fall is something that could have been avoided (e.g., by hunting on level ground), the cause of prohibition is given weight, so the ruling is haram. In contrast, if the animal falls directly to the ground after being shot and dies, the meat is halal. Even though falling to the ground is technically a cause of prohibition, it is unavoidable—the animal cannot help but fall after being shot. Therefore, that cause is disregarded, and the ruling is based on the arrow wound. The text then quotes from Al-Hidayah and expands with commentary from Al-‘Inayah and Al-Binayah. The Arabic text includes a numbered rule (37) stating: If death is certainly from the wound, the game is halal; if certainly from the fall, it is haram; if doubt exists, it is haram out of caution. The proof includes the Quranic verse from Al-Ma'idah (5:3) that prohibits mutaraddiyah (animals that fall from a height). The rational proof is that when causes conflict, the side of prohibition is preferred as a precaution, and obligation is only within capacity. The commentary also clarifies that the principle is restricted to cases where the wound is not immediately fatal. All explanations strictly follow the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
حلت (hilla): Permissibility (halal) – the legal status of an action being lawful.
حرمت (hurma): Prohibition (haram) – the legal status of an action being unlawful.
سبب (sabab): Cause – a legal cause that leads to a ruling; in this context, the cause of permissibility (the hunter's shot) and the cause of prohibition (fall into water or from height).
احتیاطاً (ihtiyātan): Out of precaution – giving precedence to the prohibition when causes conflict and avoidance is possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter shoots an arrow at a bird, and the bird is hit, then falls directly to the ground and dies, what is the ruling on eating it according to the Hanafi school?
A) Haram, because the fall is a cause of prohibition.
B) Halal, because the fall is unavoidable and the cause of prohibition is disregarded.
C) Halal only if the hunter intended to shoot it.
D) Haram, because it falls under mutaraddiyah.

Key Takeaway
When halal and haram causes combine, avoidable prohibition prevails; unavoidable prohibition is disregarded.

Gift of Connected Pawned Item Invalid
Ruling about gifted item connected to non-mortgaged property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifting a pawned item that is physically connected to non-pawned property and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
A gift of part of a pawned item is invalid if the part cannot be separately possessed.

This passage from Al-Hidayah and Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira presents a key principle in the chapter of pawn (rahn). It addresses a situation where a person attempts to give a pawned item as a gift, but that item is physically connected to something that is not pawned. The ruling is clear: such a gift is invalid. Let us understand the reasoning behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving a pawned item as a gift (hiba) when the item is physically connected (muttasil) to a non-pawned item. The ruling is that it is not valid (lam yajuz).
The Arabic 'lam yajuz' indicates the transaction is batil (void) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Find the reason (ta'lil)
The passage states the reason: 'because it is not possible to possess the mortgaged item alone' (li-annahu la yumkin qabd al-marhun wahdahu). Possession (qabd) is a condition for the validity of a gift; without the ability to take exclusive possession, the gift fails.
The condition of qabd is crucial in Hanafi hiba.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that a gift must involve the transfer of exclusive possession. If the gifted item is inseparably mixed with something else, the donee cannot take possession of only the gifted part, making the gift invalid.
This is an application of the maxim 'ma la yumkin al-qabd la yasihh al-hiba' (what cannot be possessed cannot be validly gifted).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في معنى الشائع فصار الأصل أن الموهوب إذا كان متصلا بما ليس بمرهون لم يجز، لأنه لا يمكن قبض المرهون وحده . الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الرهن، ج ١ ص ٢٢٩) الهداية: كتاب الرهن، باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره، ج ٤ ص ٥٤٧
In the sense of the shared [property], it became an established principle that if the gifted item is connected to something that is not mortgaged, it is not valid, because it is not possible to possess the mortgaged item alone. Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira: Kitab al-Rahn, vol. 1, p. 229) Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Rahn, chapter on transacting in the pawn and crimes against it and its crime against others, vol. 4, p. 547.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents a subsidiary ruling from the chapter on pawn (rahin) concerning a situation where a pawned item is physically connected to something else that is not pawned. The rule states that if a person wants to give the pawned part as a gift (hiba), it is not valid because the mortgagee cannot take exclusive possession (qabd) of the pawned part alone, due to its connection with the non-pawned property. The citation from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira and Al-Hidayah confirms this principle. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that valid possession of a gift requires the ability to isolate the gifted item, which is impossible here.

Key Terms
الشَّائِع (ash-shā’i‘): Shared property, i.e., property that is physically mixed or connected.
مُتَّصِل (muttasil): Physically connected, attached.
قَبْض (qabḍ): Taking possession; a condition for validity of gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The debt would be cancelled.
D) The gift requires a witness.

Key Takeaway
A gift of a pawned item is invalid if it is physically inseparable from non-pawned property, because separate possession is impossible.

Depreciation of Pawned Property Does Not Cancel Debt
Ruling about depreciation not cancelling debt with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that depreciation of pawned property does not cancel the debt, explain why destruction does cancel it, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf with Zufar's opposing view.

Core Idea
Only destruction of the pawn cancels the debt; depreciation does not affect the mortgagee's right.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling within the Hanafi school regarding pawn (rahn). The passage clarifies that a decrease in the market value of the pawned item does not extinguish the debt, contrary to the opinion of Imam Zufar. Through an illustrative example, we see the practical distinction between mere depreciation and actual destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'The decrease in terms of price does not cause the cancellation of the debt according to us.' This is the core ruling. Note that 'according to us' refers to the majority Hanafi position.
2
State the Hanafi position and the dispute
The text contrasts 'according to us' with 'contrary to Zufar'. Identify that Zufar, a prominent Hanafi disciple, held that depreciation cancels the debt proportionally. The dispute is intra-madhhab.
Zufar's full argument is not quoted here.
3
Understand the proof by example
The passage provides a scenario: a slave pawned for 1000, price drops to 100, then the slave is accidentally killed and compensation of 100 is paid. At maturity, the mortgagee takes the 100 as payment and demands nothing more. This shows that destruction cancels the debt (the pawn is gone), but mere depreciation does not.
The example from Majma' al-Damanat illustrates the consequence of destruction, not depreciation.
4
Distinguish depreciation from destruction
Depreciation is a decrease in market value while the pawn remains intact. Destruction (halak) is the physical loss of the pawn. Only destruction cancels the debt because the security is lost; depreciation does not affect the mortgagee's right to full repayment when the pawn is returned.
This distinction is key to the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Since depreciation does not cancel debt, the mortgagee can demand full repayment upon maturity if the pawn is intact. Under Zufar's view, the debt would be reduced proportionally. The mufta bihi (operative position) follows the majority Hanafi view.
Tarjih authority: the text indicates the majority view is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التصرف فى الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره (٣٢) النَّقْصَانُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْبَعْرِ لَا يُوجِبُ سُقُوطَ الدَّيْنِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ . قَالَ (وَمَنْ رَهَنَ عَبْدًا يُسَاوِى أَلْفًا بِأَلْفٍ ..... نُقْصَانُ الْقِيمَةِ بِتَرَاجُعِ السِّعْرِ بَعْدَ مَا قَبَضَ الرَّهْنَ لَيْسَ بِمُعْتَبِرٍ فَلَا يُوجِبُ سُقُوطَ الدَّيْنِ، وَلِهَذَا لَوْ نَقَصَ بِهِ وَهُوَ بَاقٍ عَلَى حَالِهِ فَالرَّاهِنُ يُطَالِبُ بِجَمِيعِ الدَّيْنِ عِنْدَ رَدِّ الْمُرْتَهِنِ الرَّهْنَ إِلَى الرَّاهِنِ.
