(مَجْمَعُ الضَّمَانَاتِ: كِتَابُ الرَّهْنِ، ج ا ص ١١٤)
Chapter of transacting in the pawn and crimes against it and its crime against others. (32) The decrease in terms of price does not cause the cancellation of the debt according to us, contrary to Zufar. He said: And whoever pawns a slave worth one thousand for one thousand... the decrease in value due to the decline of price after having taken possession of the pawn is not considered, so it does not cause the cancellation of the debt. Therefore, if it decreased while it remains in its condition, the pledgor is demanded for the full debt when the mortgagee returns the pawn to the pledgor. (Al-'Inayah, Kitab al-Rahn, chapter on transacting in the pawn and crimes against it and its crime against others, vol. 10, pp. 190-191) And whoever pawns a slave worth one thousand for one thousand to a term, and it decreased in price until its value returned to one hundred, then a man killed him by mistake, and paid his value of one hundred, then the term arrived, then the mortgagee takes the one hundred as payment for his right, and he does not recourse upon the pledgor for anything. (Majma' al-Damanat: Kitab al-Rahn, vol. 1, p. 114)
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding the effect of depreciation of pawned property on the debt. The text states that according to the Hanafi school (at our side), a mere decrease in the market price of the pawned item does not cause the debt to be cancelled, contrary to the opinion of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi disciple). The reasoning is that the pawn remains in the mortgagee's possession and only actual destruction (halak) of the pawn cancels the debt. Two citations are provided: from Al-'Inayah, which reiterates the principle, and from Majma' al-Damanat, which gives an example: a slave pawned for 1000, price drops to 100, then is killed accidentally; the killer pays 100 as compensation; when the loan matures, the mortgagee takes that 100 as payment and cannot claim the remaining 900 from the pledgor because the pawn has been destroyed, which does cancel the debt. The lesson thus distinguishes between mere depreciation and destruction.

Key Terms
النَّقْصَانُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْبَعْرِ (an-naqṣānu min ḥaythu al-ba‘r): Decrease in value due to market price fluctuation.
سُقُوطُ الدَّيْنِ (suqūṭ ad-dayn): Cancellation of the debt secured by the pawn.
زُفَرَ (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi scholar who differed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The debt is reduced proportionally.
B) The debt is cancelled entirely.
C) The debt remains unchanged.
D) The pawn is returned and debt forgiven.

Key Takeaway
Depreciation of pawned property does not affect the debt; only destruction cancels it.

6 min
Principle of Considering the State at the Time of the Act
Stating the maxim that ruling depends on state during act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'i'tibar halat al-fi'l' to determine liability in cases where the doer's or victim's status changes between the act and the result.

Core Idea
The act's ruling is fixed at its performance; changes after the act do not affect the doer's liability.

This lesson introduces a fundamental Hanafi principle that separates the moment of action from the moment of consequence. The passage from Al-Hidayah uses the example of an archer who shoots a Muslim target; the target apostatizes before the arrow strikes and dies as an apostate. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the shooter must pay diya because the act of shooting occurred when the target was a Muslim. We will explore why the state at the time of the act governs, not the state at death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is shooting an arrow at a person. At the moment of shooting, the target is a Muslim. Before the arrow hits, the target apostatizes and dies as an apostate.
The act is complete when the arrow leaves the bow; the result (death) occurs later.
2
State the maxim
The maxim is 'i'tibar halat al-fi'l' (consideration is for the state of the act). The ruling is based on the doer's status and the victim's status at the time the act is performed, not when the result occurs.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle.
3
Apply the maxim to determine liability
Since at the time of shooting the target was Muslim, the shooter is liable for killing a Muslim. Killing a Muslim normally warrants qisas, but here qisas is dropped due to doubt (shubha) caused by the apostasy. However, diya remains wajib because the act was committed against a Muslim.
The doubt (shubha) is the change in the victim's status, which prevents qisas but does not nullify diya.
4
Confirm the outcome
The ruling is that diya is wajib on the shooter. This illustrates the principle's operation: the state at the time of the act controls, not the state at death.
If the target had been a disbeliever at the time of shooting, no diya would be required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فى اعتبار حالة القتل
(۵۲) الْإِعْتِبَارُ لِحَالَةِ الْفِعْل.
ترجمہ: اعتبار فعل کی حالت کا ہوتا ہے۔
۲۵۳
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اسلام اور کفر کا اعتبار اس حالت کا ہوگا جس حالت میں فاعل سے فعل کا صدور ہورہا تھا، یعنی فعل کا اعتبار فاعل سے صدور فعل کی حالت کا ہوگا، مفعول پر فضل کے وقوع کی حالت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، ہم دیکھیں گے کہ جس وقت فاعل سے فعل صادر ہور ہا تھا اس وقت مفعول مسلمان تھا یا کافر ، اور اسی اعتبار سے حکم مرتب ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر رامی نے مرمی الیہ کی طرف تیر مارا اور تیر مارتے وقت مرمی الیہ مسلمان تھا، اب مرمی الیہ العیاذ باللہ تیر لگنے سے

وقوله وإذا اختلف شاهدا القتل ظاهر، وقد تقدم في الشهادات أن اختلاف الشاهدين في الأموال يمنع من الحكم بها ففى النفوس أولى. وقوله لأن المطلق يغاير المقيد فإن المطلق يوجب الدية في ماله والمقيد بالعصا على العاقلة (العناية كتاب الجنايات باب الشهادة في القتل، ج ۱۰ ص ۲۶۴ (وكذا الحكم (إذا قال أحدهما أى أحد الشاهدين قتله بعصا، وقال الآخر: لا أدرى بأى شيء قتله، فهو باطل لأن المطلق يغاير المقيد لأن المقضى به إن كان القتل بعصا فالدية على العاقلة، وإن كان المقضى به لا يعلم فالدية في ماله، كذا ذكره شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ. Chapter on consideration of the state of killing. (52) Consideration is for the state of the act. Translation: Consideration is for the state of the act. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that Islam and disbelief are considered according to the state in which the doer was performing the act. That is, the act is considered according to the state at the time of occurrence from the doer; the state in which the effect occurs on the object is not considered. We will see: at the time the doer performed the act, was the object Muslim or disbeliever? And according to that, the ruling will be applied. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, is explaining that if an archer shot an arrow at the target, and at the time of shooting the target was Muslim, then the target, God forbid, from the arrow... And his saying: 'If the two witnesses of killing differ is obvious, and it has preceded in the chapter of testimonies that the difference of two witnesses in property matters prevents judgement, so in blood matters it is more deserving.' And his saying: 'Because the absolute differs from the restricted; the absolute necessitates blood money (diya) from his own wealth, while the restricted with a stick necessitates it on the 'aqilah.' (Al-'Inayah, Kitab al-Jinayat, Bab al-Shahada fi al-Qatl, vol. 10 p. 264) And similarly the ruling: If one of the two witnesses said: 'He killed him with a stick,' and the other said: 'I do not know with what he killed him,' then it is invalid because the absolute differs from the restricted. Because if the judged matter is killing with a stick, the diya is on the 'aqilah; if the judged matter is unknown, the diya is from his own wealth. Thus mentioned by Shaykh al-Islam Khahar Zadah. (Al-Binayah, Kitab al-Jinayat, Bab al-Shahada fi al-Qatl, vol. 13 p. 152) Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Jinayat, Bab fi I'tibar Halat al-Qatl, vol. 4 p. 575. He first apostatized, then the arrow hit and he died in the state of apostasy. So according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the shooter is liable for diya. Because in the mentioned case, at the time of the act from the shooter, the target was Muslim, and consideration is for the state of the act from the doer. In the mentioned case, at the time of the act, the target was Muslim, and killing a Muslim necessitates qisas, but in this case qisas has fallen due to doubt, but diya remains wajib.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental Hanafi legal maxim: the ruling of an act is based on the doer's status at the moment of performing the act, not on the status at the time the result occurs. The example given is of an archer who shoots a Muslim target; the target apostatizes before being struck but dies as an apostate. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the shooter must pay diya to the apostate's heirs because the act of shooting occurred when the target was still a Muslim, and that is the relevant state. The passage also includes a secondary discussion about contradictory witnesses in homicide cases, but the core principle is clear: the doer's status at the time of the act governs.

Key Terms
اعتبار حالة الفعل (i'tibār ḥālat al-fi'l): The principle that legal rulings are based on the doer's status (e.g., Muslim or kafir) at the time of performing the act, not at the time the result occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim archer shoots an arrow at another Muslim. Before the arrow hits, the target apostatizes and dies as an apostate. According to the principle in this passage, what is the ruling for the archer?
A) No liability because the victim died as an apostate.
B) Diya is wajib because the shooting occurred when the target was Muslim.
C) Qisas is wajib because the act was intentional.
D) The archer is free because the target's apostasy nullifies liability.

Key Takeaway
The state at the time of the act determines the ruling; subsequent changes do not affect the doer's liability.
